**Done in previous sessions (Graph quality — Sessions 68–100).**

- **2026-07-23 — Session 100: Graph-quality S7 shipped, and a follow-up that made the name-normalisation queue actually usable (PRs #222 + #223, both squash-merged; Graph-quality S0–S7 now complete).** S7 was planned as "fill the gaps in the reader's correction surface". The survey found there were none: right-clicking a highlighted entity already offered every correction the spec describes, and the entity picker already searched *every* entity in the project rather than only the ones appearing in the story being read — confirmed in the browser by re-assigning to a character who exists solely in a sibling story. So the slice did something else instead. The specification had promised, since the beginning, that hovering an entity would show "a brief description" — but no entity has ever had a description; the field does not exist anywhere in the system, and the architecture notes had quietly resolved that two months ago without anyone updating the spec. Rather than delete the promise, the owner chose to **derive** one from the graph: hovering now shows up to three of an entity's connections, most-connected first, with a "+N more" line. Two ride-alongs shipped with it — the review queues gained a "3 of 12 remaining" position indicator, and their empty states gained a link onward through the curation flow, replacing four dead ends. **Working the real graph afterwards was where most of the session's value came from.** It exposed that one screen took fourteen seconds to reload after every decision, which — because the queue reloads after *every* decision — meant deciding a few items in quick succession exhausted the browser's connection limit and made the entire application appear broken. Nothing was wrong: no errors, the server answering in milliseconds, every decision saved. It was fixed by remembering the label embeddings instead of recomputing all 272 of them each time (fourteen seconds → 1.4). **A second fix in that follow-up was built, reviewed, and then reverted before merge** — removing a decided row from the list immediately felt better, but the queue tracks the highlighted row by *position*, so making the list change 300× sooner moved a dormant bug into the window where the author is still typing, where a keystroke could land on a row that had just shifted. It is backlogged with the reason and the prerequisite, since the same hazard exists in all four queues. **Both PRs went through both review gates, and the heavier multi-agent review found real bugs the self-review missed on each** — including, in the first, that the fix for the tooltip's ordering had been applied to what the reader *sees* but not to the calculation ranking it, and that the test written to guard that ordering could not actually fail. **Four follow-ups were opened from simply using the thing:** the name-normalisation screen asks whether two labels mean the same thing while showing nothing about what either one connects (dumping the underlying links answered a question the owner couldn't); **24 % of the graph is completely disconnected** — 39 of 161 entities, with two thirds of the graph attached by at most one link — with no way to clean them in bulk; the queue-cursor prerequisite above; and, recorded against the upcoming roadmap decision rather than the backlog, a note to **run fresh sample text through the whole pipeline before choosing what to build next**, because the current graph has been hand-cleaned across four slices and no longer reflects what the pipeline actually produces. **Retro (owner ran `/retro`, three changes approved):** the review skill gained a lens for sweeping a *conceptual* mistake through the rest of its own function rather than fixing only the visible symptom; the root instructions gained a rule to **measure a reported slowness before judging it**, since "takes a moment" and "stalls the whole app" read identically in prose and took thirty seconds to tell apart; and the backend notes now record that throwaway database scripts must suppress their errors, because the driver prints the full connection string — including the password — on the most ordinary mistakes. **Checks:** 738 backend + 542 frontend tests, all linting/typing/formatting clean, CI green on both PRs. **Next: the milestone roll** — Graph-quality is complete and closing.

- **2026-07-23 — Session 99: Cleared both security-gate reds on `main` — every backend OSV waiver dropped by a real fix, and a neo4j image bump that retired six more (config-only; PR #220, squash-merged).** A security session that opened on a red scheduled `main` run, exactly as the previous session's time-box was designed to force. The setuptools advisory's waiver expired on schedule, and this time the real fix was available: torch 2.13.0 had cleared its 14-day soak that same morning, and because it drops torch's cap on setuptools it unblocked the setuptools upgrade that had been stuck for a week. Both landed together. A bonus fell out — torch 2.13.0 turns out to carry no known advisory at all, so the long-standing torch waiver lost its justification too, leaving the backend dependency scanner running with **no waivers whatsoever** for the first time: every advisory that gate has ever raised has ended in a fix rather than a permanent exception. Fixing that red then exposed a second, unrelated one that had been hidden behind it (the job stops at the first failure, so the image scans never ran): six new high-severity advisories in Java libraries bundled inside the Neo4j image. No Neo4j release fixes them — not even one published the day before — so they needed owner-approved exceptions, each with a written justification for why it cannot be reached here (three are in a protocol Neo4j does not implement; one needs a compression format it never negotiates; one is in an authentication scheme it does not use; one needs untrusted JSON it never receives). But the investigation also found that upgrading the image to a three-week-old release would *fix* six advisories we had been ignoring since May — so the upgrade rode along, and those six exceptions were deleted rather than carried. A scan diff confirmed the upgrade introduced nothing new. Full CI passed, including all three image scans, and the integration suite ran green against the new image. **Retro (owner ran `/retro`):** the session exposed a structural hole — exceptions that expire on a *date* re-break CI automatically, but exceptions that wait on *"a fixed version being published"* had no working check at all. Both rituals said to re-check them by re-running the scan, but that only ever scans the version currently pinned, which will carry its advisory forever; the condition could therefore never be observed as met. That is why six of them sat unnecessary for three weeks. Both skills were corrected to check the newest *available* version instead, and a two-second freshness check was added to the session-start ritual — which on its very first run flagged two further images running versions many weeks behind available rebuilds, now tracked as a follow-up. **The Graph-quality build is untouched — S7 stays next.** **Next: Graph-quality S7 — reader as a correction surface for existing entities — a fresh conversation.**

- **2026-07-21 — Session 98: Cleared a fresh security-gate red on `main` — setuptools OSV waiver extended + unmasked ollama x/image HIGHs waived (config-only; PR #218, squash-merged).** A between-build-units security session prompted by `/resume-session` §3b flagging the setuptools OSV waiver past its floor — the scheduled `main` run had re-reddened the backend SCA gate. The plan was to *drop* the waiver by bumping to the fixed `setuptools==83.0.0`, but that fix is forbidden by `torch==2.12.0`, which caps `setuptools<82` (the resolver fails); the only torch that relaxes it (2.13.0) is two days shy of its 14-day soak. Bumping torch young was rejected — the dependency-age CI gate has no exception, so it would just trade one red for another — so the waiver was *extended* to torch 2.13.0's soak floor (2026-07-23), with a note recording the combined bump due then. Fixing the OSV red then **unmasked** a fresh Trivy red on the ollama image (the security job scans OSV before the images, so a red OSV step had hidden the ollama scan for days): two `golang.org/x/image` TIFF-decoder denial-of-service HIGHs compiled into the ollama binary. Per the project's "two independent reds on one required gate must be fixed together" rule they rode the same PR — an owner-approved HIGH waiver on the same reasoning as the ~20 existing ollama Go-library waivers (unreachable on a single-user loopback deployment; only an upstream ollama rebuild ships the fix). All four waiver files were kept mirrored; local OSV and Trivy re-scans were clean, and the full CI `security` job went green on the PR and again on `main` after merge. Config-only, so `/review-pr` was the gate (no `/code-review`). **Retro (owner ran `/retro`):** hardened `/triage-advisory` so a sub-soak dependency bump is never offered as a way to green CI (the age gate has no per-package exception; the only green paths are wait-for-soak or waive) — the same "verify the option's real constraints before putting the choice to the owner" lesson S97 earned in a different form. **The Graph-quality build is untouched — S7 stays next.** **Next: Graph-quality S7 — reader as a correction surface for existing entities — a fresh conversation.**
- **2026-07-20 — Session 97: Graph-quality S6c BUILT — the label name-scorer subset over-match tune (PR #216, squash-merged).** The backend precision tune the owner split out of S6b. The name-normalisation review list was noisy because its name-similarity rung scored a short label 100 whenever it was a token-subset of a longer one: on the real graph a bare predicate `IN` (one use) scored a perfect name-match against `STORED_IN`, `STORES_IN`, and every other `…_IN` predicate, so the list drowned in false pairs where only the embedding score separated them. The fix adds a subset-**intolerant** scorer (RapidFuzz `token_sort_ratio`, which is length-aware — `in` vs `stored in` scores ~36, not 100) and routes only the label self-join through it. **The decision that shaped the session was *where* to apply it:** a grep of the shared scorer's consumers before any code found that it is also the live extraction matcher (where a partial name matching an honorific — `Bronek`→`Stary Bronek` — is a *wanted* behaviour, tuned against the spec), not just the duplicate-entity finder the handoff named. So the fix was kept at the label layer, leaving the shared scorer untouched — surfaced to the owner, who reversed an initial "change the shared one" call once the third consumer was known. Built test-first; the multi-agent `/code-review` caught a real edge-case regression (two junk labels that both normalise to empty scored 100 under the new scorer where the old one scored 0) which was guarded and tested. Live-verified on the real Oakhaven graph (227 predicates / 45 types): the 13 bare-`IN` false pairs drop to zero and every genuine spelling/casing variant is preserved. 712 backend tests pass; ruff + mypy clean; CI green; no spec amendment, no ADR. **Retro (owner ran `/retro`):** the friction was surfacing the where-to-fix decision to the owner *before* doing the cheap grep that establishes the real blast radius, which turned one decision into two; hardened into `/resume-session` §4 — the existing "a handoff's list is keyword-derived, verify before trusting" rule now explicitly covers a handoff's "shared with X" note about a code primitive (grep every consumer before deciding where to change it). **Next: S7 — reader as a correction surface for existing entities — a fresh conversation.**
- **2026-07-16 — Session 96: Graph-quality S6b BUILT — the `/stories/:id/normalise-names` frontend list (PR #214, squash-merged).** The frontend half of name-normalisation: a dedicated review screen that surfaces the shipped S6a suggestions so the author can clean a noisy over-extracted vocabulary. It mirrors the S4b duplicates list — two grouped sections (predicate names, entity-type names) under one keyboard cursor, each pair showing an honest name-match/embedding score and per-form use-counts; the author picks a form to keep (arming a graph-wide rename with a "fold N edges" preview, then a confirm), or dismisses the pair as "not synonyms" with an Undo. Pure frontend over the already-shipped endpoints — no backend change — built test-first by reusing the shared review-queue hook and the duplicates pattern. Both review gates caught real defects the build missed and both were folded: the self-`/review-pr` found that a rename is a graph write and so must refresh the graph/reader/detail caches (not just its own list), and the required multi-agent `/code-review` found an empty error banner on a network-level failure, two status banners that stacked instead of replacing each other, and a hand-typed union that should derive from the schema. One duplication cleanup (a `clamp` helper now copied across four review screens) was consciously deferred to `docs/BACKLOG.md` rather than scope-creep three untouched features. 532 frontend tests pass; lint + build clean; CI green; no spec amendment, no ADR. **Browser-smoke-verified on the real Oakhaven graph**, which confirmed the feature works *and* exposed two things: the predicate name-scorer's over-match (a bare `IN` scoring a perfect name-match against every `…_IN` predicate) — split out as **S6c**, its own backend tuning unit — and a dev-setup gap. **Retro (owner ran `/retro`):** the smoke lost time to a 500 because the embedding library lives in a separate `embeddings` dependency group that `backend/AGENTS.md`'s run instructions never mentioned (they only said `--group models`); both "Running locally" and the manual-smoke block now install `--group models --group embeddings`. Also noted as follow-ups (not process changes): whether the S6a label-vocabulary route should degrade to name-only when the embedding model is absent instead of returning a bare 500. **Next: S6c — the predicate name-scorer precision tune (backend, test-first) — a fresh conversation.**
- **2026-07-15 — Session 95: Graph-quality S6a-2 BUILT — the two graph-write name-normalisation apply ops + endpoint (PR #212, squash-merged).** The write/apply half of S6, the risky part the owner split out (S92) for a focused review. Built test-first behind the S6a-1 suggestions: a graph-wide **predicate rename** (re-keys every bearing edge in one grouped, reversible operation, preserving each edge's surrogate handle and folding identical triples with a reported count — reuses the shipped single-edge re-key machinery, so no new graph-write symbol) and a graph-wide **entity-type relabel** (the one net-new writer, a bulk `SET n.type`, recorded per node so undo restores each exactly), both reachable only from one new human endpoint `POST /stories/{id}/label-vocabulary/rename` (surface-discriminated, story lookup inside the 503 guard). Verified end-to-end against real Neo4j + Postgres: N-edge undo as one atom, fold-then-unfold, Cypher-hostile label injection-safety, exact type-relabel undo, and no node-collapse on a relabel to a pre-existing type. `/review-pr` clean; the required multi-agent `/code-review` caught a real bug the self-pass missed — the request validator stripped `from_label`, so a rename could never target a stored label with surrounding whitespace (the exact messy case normalisation exists to clean) — fixed, plus a redundant-guard cleanup; two undo-integrity windows were documented as the accepted single-author last-write-wins posture (identical to the existing merge/delete pattern) rather than re-architected. `invariants.md` updated (INV-9 grew by the one new writer symbol — 8th witnessed path; INV-10 marked realized-consumer). 700 backend tests green; ruff + mypy clean; no spec amendment, no new ADR. Retro: reflective pass found the session validated existing process (test-first, plan-mode multi-`Explore` reuse-mapping, and the required `/code-review` again catching a real functional bug on substantive code); the only recurring friction was iterating on ruff's 100-char line limit in dense docstrings — execution discipline, not a process gap — so nothing cleared the bar for a rule/skill change. **Next: S6b — the `/stories/:id/normalise-names` frontend list.**
- **2026-07-15 — Session 94: Cleared a fresh OSV security-gate red on `main` — time-boxed setuptools waiver (PR #210, squash-merged).** A between-build-units session prompted by the owner ("check CI on main, something new emerged"): the scheduled `main` CI run had reddened the backend OSV SCA gate on a newly-surfaced MEDIUM advisory (GHSA-h35f-9h28-mq5c / CVE-2026-59890 / PYSEC-2026-3447) against unchanged deps — `setuptools` 81.0.0's `MANIFEST.in` exclude directives lack Unicode normalization, so on macOS APFS/HFS+ an NFD name can slip into an sdist. `/triage-advisory` decided a **time-boxed waiver** over a fix: the fix (83.0.0) exists but was published 2026-07-04, still inside the 14-day soak on 2026-07-15, so a bump would break §6.7. - **2026-07-15 — Session 93: Logged a backlog course-correction — the tooling-extraction *copy-model is wrong; we need a generator* (docs-only, no code).** A single clarify-and-log session between build units. - **2026-07-13 — Session 92: Graph-quality S6a-1 BUILT — name-normalisation backend, read/suggest half (PR #207, squash-merged).** The first build unit after the S6 register resolved (S91). A build-time check on the real Oakhaven graph (227 predicates / 45 types) confirmed the embedding rung earns its place — it uniquely catches `LOCATION`↔`PLACE` (a genuine synonym plain spelling-match misses) — so it ships. - **2026-07-13 — Session 90: Graph-quality S6 decomposed — step-0 architecture, register OPEN (PR #203, squash-merged).** Back in the Graph-quality sequence after the tooling-extraction detour. Ran the `meta-architect:decompose-requirement` step-0 for **S6 — predicate- AND entity-type-name normalisation + synonym suggestion**: one human-gated *suggest-then-you-decide* pass that will let the author normalise the noisy vocabulary of an over-extracted graph — both the relationship names (`PASSENGER_ON`→`ON_SHIP`) and the entity-type labels (`PERSON`/`Person`, `GROUP`/`group`/…) — with an NLP/embedding layer *suggesting* which names look synonymous and the human deciding each rename (nothing auto-collapses; INV-4). The deliverable is the vault proposal `architecture/proposals/graph-name-normalisation.md` (nine-layer + nine-station pass, an operation-surface completeness sweep, a data-flow diagram, an edge-case enumeration, and the register **DM-NN-1..6** left OPEN for the owner) — **no production code, no spec or plan change.** The architectural payoff was answering the task's central "one engine or two?" at the *storage* layer via a reuse-first code survey: a predicate is stored as the Neo4j relationship type (so renaming it re-keys every edge and rides the `edge_uid` handle S5 reserved), while an entity type is a plain node property (so renaming it is a bulk relabel) — hence **one shared "find the synonyms" engine + two different "do the rename" actions**, not two whole engines nor one leaky one. Added the `controlled-vocabulary` glossary term. Vault-only, so `/review-pr` was the gate (no `/code-review`); the self-review caught and folded one overspecified invariant-count claim. **Retro (owner ran full `/retro`):** turned the caught-twice claim into a standing `architecture/AGENTS.md` convention (proposals don't assert an exact *forward* invariant-enumeration ordinal — the build assigns it). **Next: the owner resolves the S6 register (DM-NN-1..6), one plain-language question at a time, in a fresh conversation; the build slices follow.**

- **2026-07-10 — Session 82: Graph-quality S5b-be — the edge-write backend, BUILT (production code; PR #188, squash-merged).** The first edge-*write* slice: a stable `edge_uid` surrogate handle + an atomic server-side edge re-key (edit-predicate / re-target), consuming spec §4's reserved handle so a future relation qualifier / reification can outlive ordinary curation. Story Forge edges are content-addressed (`relation_edge_id = uuid5(subject, predicate, object)`), so changing a predicate or endpoint **re-keys** the edge — until now faked client-side as remove-old + add-new, which mints a new edge each time and drops anything attached to it. **What shipped:** (1) `GraphRelation.edge_uid` (a `uuid4`, default `None`) stored **only** as a Neo4j edge property (via `create_relation`'s `MERGE … ON CREATE SET`, whose no-`ON MATCH` semantics *are* the coalesce rule) — so **no Alembic migration** (`staged_relations` is content-`edge_id`-keyed, untouched); minted forward on every edge writer (relation-decide commit, `add_relation`, the re-key), never back-filled. (2) A pure `domain/relation_rekey.py` (`plan_relation_rekey`, mirroring `plan_merge`'s re-point classification) + `EntityEditService.retarget_relation` doing create-new-then-delete-old as one grouped reversible op preserving the handle (fold onto a collision keeps the survivor's own handle); it **reuses the merge writer's `repoint_relation`/`fold_relation` op-strings**, so `graph_undo` already inverts it (undo restores predicate **and** handle). (3) `PATCH /stories/{id}/relations/{edge_id}` (`RetargetRelationRequest`, ≥1 field; empty body → 422; 404 stale edge / missing endpoint) + OpenAPI & typed-client regen. (4) **ADR 0011** (escalated form — data-model identity boundary) + **INV-10** ("an edge's `edge_uid` survives re-point/re-predicate/merge") minted with enforcer + tests; INV-9 grep set **unchanged** (7th witnessed instance — reuses `create`/`delete_relation`, so only the reachable path grows). Test-first throughout: pure planner → real-Neo4j round-trip + the ON-CREATE coalesce → service-with-fakes + undo round-trips → **real-store end-to-end** (re-key preserves the handle, undo restores it) → API contract; the producer↔inverter contract driven from the re-key's *real* rows. **Reviewed** with `/review-pr` **and** the required multi-agent `/code-review` (high, 6 verified findings, 0 refuted) — the second gate caught a real **data-loss bug the self-review missed** (and had reasoned past): the re-key deleted the old edge *before* creating the new one as two separate Neo4j transactions, so a store failure between them lost the edge entirely → **reordered to create-first** (a mid-failure now leaves a recoverable duplicate, never a missing edge — closing the very no-edge window DM-S5-2 chose the atomic op to avoid). Four more findings folded (an honest crash-window docstring + ADR; a domain blank-predicate guard closing an asymmetry `model_copy` opened; the stale `AddRelationRequest` docstring; skip redundant endpoint reads); one deferred per rule-of-three. **630 tests green** (both tiers), ruff + mypy `--strict` clean, all CI green. **Two follow-ups tracked** (both pre-existing, split out per the merge-flow rule): the `get_story`-outside-the-503-guard systemic gap across all edit routes → cross-cutting; `merge_entities`' edge re-point sharing the same delete-first data-loss window → `docs/BACKLOG.md`. **Retro:** skipped (owner) — the reflection confirmed the required-`/code-review` rule earned its keep again; nothing actionable for the process. **Next: Graph-quality S5b-fe** (the canvas edge affordances — edit-predicate / re-target / delete on the panel, driving the new PATCH op).

- **2026-07-01 — Session 75: Graph-quality S3a — backend edge-evidence + verifiable-merge reads (production code; PR #172, squash-merged).** Built the two read surfaces the resolved S3 register scopes (DM-EE-1/2/3), test-first, backend-only. A new `PostgresRelationStore.get_written_by_edge_id` (+ an `edge_id` index migration) + a pure `domain/edge_evidence.py` assembly back `GET /stories/{id}/relations/{edge_id}/evidence`, which returns an edge's predicate + every `written` source paragraph/quote (one-to-many; a manually-added edge → 200 + empty "added manually", not 404). `CandidateView` gained `target_canonical_name` + a typed `AlternativeView` (type/aliases/sample context quote), batched to avoid an N+1; enrichment is best-effort so a graph-DB outage degrades to an unenriched queue rather than blocking the human review. Pure boundaries unit-tested, store + routes integration-tested; OpenAPI regenerated (`openapi.json` + `schema.d.ts`). **Reviewed** with `/review-pr` (caught a blocking frontend-CI break — the typed `alternatives` contract broke two test fixtures, the §2 "changed shape has consumers" hazard — plus `docs/code` reference drift; both folded) **and** multi-agent `/code-review` at high (caught a real availability regression — a Neo4j outage 503'ing the whole Postgres-backed queue — two undeclared-500 error-contract holes, and an N+1; all folded with tests). Backend 573 + frontend 341 tests pass; mypy/ruff/build clean; all CI green. **Lesson (retro → applied):** the self-`/review-pr` dismissed the contract holes as "matches the existing pattern" and missed the availability regression the second gate caught — so a new `/review-pr` §4 lens now names the inverse contract-hole (a declared-503 route must route *every* store read through the guard; a sibling sharing the gap is not a clearance), and this is another data point toward making `/code-review` a required gate for substantive backend code (S51 question). **Next: Graph-quality S3b** (frontend edge-tap + `EdgeEvidencePanel` + merge-context render + the DM-EE-4/5 safeguards + the amber-highlight fix).
- **2026-07-01 — Session 74: Graph-quality S3 (Edge evidence + verifiable merges) DECOMPOSED + register RESOLVED + merged (PR #170; architecture/planning, no production code).** Ran `meta-architect:decompose-requirement` on the branchy S3 slice → `architecture/proposals/graph-edge-evidence.md` (nine-layer pass, operation-surface sweep, data-flow Mermaid, register DM-EE-1..6 / OQ-31, "but what if", plain-language owner gaps); the owner resolved the register the same conversation, one question at a time. **Defining finding (grounded by two parallel `Explore` code-survey agents):** S3 is a **read/verify** slice whose data is *real but not on the wire* — edge **provenance** (source paragraph(s) + `evidence_quote`) survives commit in Postgres `staged_relations` (`status='written'`, keyed by the content-addressed `edge_id`) but reaches no client and has **no by-`edge_id` read or index** (`postgres_relation_store.py:94-112`); `GraphCanvas` taps **nodes only** (`GraphCanvas.tsx:106`); the merge surfaces show a bare `(100)` + a generic "an existing entity" (`CandidateView` has no `target_canonical_name`). So S3's real work is a small set of new **read** surfaces, **not** new storage and **not** the §4 write-handle. **S3 writes nothing** — INV-1/3/9 untouched; INV-4 constrains DM-EE-4. **Resolutions (owner — every entry on the leaner option, a coherent "leaner reads, verify by evidence" cut):** DM-EE-1 focused per-edge BFF evidence read (fetch-on-tap); DM-EE-2 all `written` `staged_relations` by `edge_id` (+ index; zero-provenance → "added manually"); DM-EE-3 enrich all merge surfaces (type+aliases+quote+`target_canonical_name` — **closes the cross-cutting `CandidateView`-no-target-name item at the S3a build**); DM-EE-4 solve the score-100 trap by context, not type-classification (INV-4-safe); DM-EE-5 client-side warn-and-offer dup-create gate; DM-EE-6 backend-first (S3a) / frontend-second (S3b, amber-highlight fix rides). **No spec amendment; no ADR.** Added the `provenance` glossary term (30→31). **Handoff correction:** the S73 handoff's "S3 consumes the reserved §4 edge handle" was drift — code-verified no surrogate handle is built; S3 reads by the content id (the handle is an edge-*write* concern, S5/S6). **Reviewed** with `/review-pr` (clean — §2 reconciliation verified home-by-home; one INDEX nit folded); CI green (docs-PR shape: code jobs path-skipped, secret-scan + CodeQL green). Reconciled across `architecture/` (proposal → accepted, OQ-31 struck, INDEX, CHANGELOG, glossary) + `docs/PLAN_SHORT.md` Decided S74. **Next: build Graph-quality S3a** (backend-first, test-first — the `staged_relations`-by-`edge_id` read + `edge_id` index, and the `CandidateView` enrichment + `target_canonical_name`).
- **2026-07-01 — Session 73: Graph-quality S2 — navigate the graph, BUILT (PR #168 merged; the milestone's first navigation slice).** A dense graph (real Oakhaven: 186 nodes / 286 edges, 46 type variants) was an unnavigable `cose` hairball; S2 makes it navigable, **client-side over the payload already fetched** (no backend/schema/endpoint/LLM change; read-only, INV-1/3/9 untouched). Shipped (spec §3.4, `frontend/src/AGENTS.md` test-first): a pure `graphFilters.ts` — `nodeDegrees`/`elementDegrees`/`distinctTypes`/`filterGraph` (AND-combine type + connection-density) + diacritic-folding `matchNodes` — plus a shared `useDebouncedValue` hook, all unit-tested first; `GraphViewer` runs the pipeline and hands a filtered element set + search-match ids to a thin `GraphCanvas`, which swaps `cose` → the **`cytoscape-fcose`** layout extension. Filters hide-and-relayout the visible subset; name search highlights + pans-to (never a hard filter); "0 of N — clear filters" and "match hidden by active filters" affordances; selection clears when a filter hides the selected node; type options prune gracefully across a refetch. **Reviewed** with `/review-pr` (self) **and** multi-agent `/code-review` (high) — the latter caught **4 real findings the self-pass missed/dismissed** (minDegree clamp, single degree source, message conflict, helper reuse), all folded with new tests. **`cytoscape-fcose@2.2.0`** pinned via `/add-dependency` (1260 d old, OSV-clean). **Browser-smoke-verified at Oakhaven scale** — which caught a real layout bug (`randomize:false` clumped the graph; fixed to `randomize:true`); all filters/search/affordances confirmed live. **Green:** 341 frontend tests, tsc/eslint/prettier/dep-age all clean, CI fully green (code-bearing PR — frontend/backend/security/CodeQL all pass). Refreshed `docs/code/frontend-features.md` for the new modules. Two follow-ups filed to `docs/BACKLOG.md` (URL-persist graph view state; label crowding on an all-disconnected filtered set). **Process (retro):** root `AGENTS.md` gains a carve-out — `/wrap-session` is not a deferrable unit; it closes its session in the *same* conversation. **Next: Graph-quality S3** (edge evidence + verifiable merges).
- **2026-06-29 — Session 72: Graph-quality S2 (Navigate the graph) decomposed + register RESOLVED + merged (PR #166; architecture/planning, no production code).** Ran `meta-architect:decompose-requirement` on the branchy S2 navigate slice → `architecture/proposals/graph-navigation.md` (nine layers, stations mostly `n/a` — read-only, data-flow Mermaid, register DM-GN-1..4 / OQ-30, the "but what if" pass, a build hand-off). The owner resolved the register the same conversation (see Decided S72). **Defining finding (completeness sweep):** every §3.4 filter runs **client-side over the payload `useStoryGraph` already fetches** — `GraphNode` carries `type`+names+aliases, node degree derives from `edges[]`, the "by story" axis is already shipped as the binary `scope` toggle — so S2 is a clean read-only, frontend-led slice (no new backend; INV-1/3/9 untouched; INV-4 constrains the type filter). **Resolutions:** DM-GN-1 client-side filtering; DM-GN-2 `cytoscape-fcose` layout (pin at build); DM-GN-3 spec-faithful — S2 navigation-only, the edge-tap evidence panel stays S3; DM-GN-4 AND-combine + hide-and-relayout + search-as-focus. **DM-GN-3 caught and reconciled a real spec↔vault drift** — the accepted parent `graph-curation-surface` proposal had claimed the edge panel was "S2's"; per the source-wins rule that note was the drift and was fixed (its §3 operation-sweep + cross-refs → S3), plus a tiny spec §4 wording fix ("S2's edge surface" → "the S3+ edge slices respect it") with owner OK. **Reviewed** with `/review-pr` (clean — the §2 reconciliation sweep verified the decision resolved in every home); CI green (docs-PR shape: code jobs path-skipped, secret-scan + CodeQL green). **Process (retro):** added a root `AGENTS.md` Merge-flow rule + a `/resume-session` pointer — **branch before the first edit of a unit, and announce the plan** — after the whole S2 decompose ran as uncommitted edits on `main` until the owner asked whether it had been branched/PR'd. **Next: build Graph-quality S2** (frontend-led, test-first — pure filter/degree/search functions, then UI, then the `/add-dependency` `cytoscape-fcose` swap, browser-smoke-verified).
- **2026-06-29 — Session 71: Graph-quality S1 — stopped silent data loss in the auto-chunker (PR #164 merged; the first build slice of the milestone).** The auto-chunker (and per-span hybrid) could drop trailing paragraphs or leave a gap and report success, silently losing text — and 502'd with no retry on a trivial off-by-one overshoot. Fix (spec `docs/specs/graph-quality.md` §3 S1, TDD failing-test-first): one canonical range invariant `domain.paragraph_range_problem` (overshoot **or** a coverage hole; overlap allowed — duplication, not loss) folded into the agent's retried validation via a new optional `check` hook on `validate_with_retry`, so **both** a coverage gap and an overshoot **re-prompt** rather than fail; the coordinator re-asserts it as a terminal `OutlineCoverageError` backstop (→ the route's already-declared 502). No API/OpenAPI/migration change. **Reviewed** with `/review-pr` (clean) + multi-agent `/code-review` (high, 35 agents): the review caught the original recovery *asymmetry* (overshoot retried, coverage hard-failed) — the owner chose **option B** (symmetric retry), which also resolved the duplicate-overshoot-rule finding via the shared domain home; two doc homes reconciled, overlap-rejection deferred to `docs/BACKLOG.md`. **Live-verified** on the branch before merge: a real Ollama Cloud `auto` chunk (5 paragraphs in → 5 persisted, no loss — the auto path's first live exercise) + a controlled-provider demo through the real wired code showing re-prompt-then-recover, give-up→502, and the coordinator backstop→502. Test data cleaned up by exact id afterward. **Green:** 555 backend tests pass, ruff/mypy clean, CI fully green. **Process (retro):** added a `backend/AGENTS.md` rule for live-test data hygiene (disposable name + delete-by-id) after the test story collided by name with the owner's real `oakhaven` graph. **Next: Graph-quality S2** (navigate the graph — filters + search + a better layout).
- **2026-06-27 — Session 70: a security-treadmill maintenance pass — dropped the starlette waiver and waived a fresh ollama CVE, folded into one PR by a required-gate constraint (PR #161 merged; no production-logic code).** `/resume-session` step 3b flagged the starlette OSV waiver as due on its 2026-06-27 floor; `/triage-advisory` drove the drop — bumped `starlette` 1.2.0 → 1.3.1 (`/add-dependency`; 15-day soak, OSV-clean, age-gate green, 363 unit tests green, app imports), clearing CVE-2026-54283 (HIGH DoS) + CVE-2026-54282 (LOW) at the source and removing both `[[IgnoredVulns]]` blocks + the `WAIVERS.md` section. Opening the PR surfaced an **unrelated** fresh red: `ollama/ollama:0.24.0` carried a new `golang.org/x/crypto/ssh/agent` HIGH (**CVE-2026-39832**), waived (owner-approved §6.7) on the same unreachability as its 8 wave-6 ssh siblings (ollama opens no SSH agent client). The discovery that **`main` was double-red on the *required* `security` gate** — the starlette waiver having *expired* on its `ignoreUntil` floor that very day, plus the ollama CVE — meant neither single-fix PR could go green (each left the other red), so #162 (ollama) was folded into #161 (starlette) and the two landed as one combined PR. `/review-pr` clean on the starlette change; CI green after a Docker-Hub-flake re-run. **Process lesson (retro):** dropping a waiver on its floor date can collide with another treadmill red on the same required gate → `/triage-advisory` now scans for a second `security` red before dropping, and root `AGENTS.md` Merge-flow gains the "two unrelated reds on one required gate → combine" exception. **Also landed the long-uncommitted Session 69 S0 work in this same wrap** (it had been done in a prior conversation but never committed). **Lesson:** the resume ritual earned its keep twice — it flagged the due waiver *and* caught that a whole prior session (S0) sat uncommitted with a stale handoff. **Next: Graph-quality S1** (the chunker completeness check — first build slice).
- **2026-06-26 — Session 69: Graph-quality S0 decompose — the in-place graph-curation surface designed and the milestone reshaped (architecture/planning; no production code; landed 2026-06-27 with the Session 70 wrap).** Ran `meta-architect:decompose-requirement` on "the graph view as a direct in-place curation surface" → `architecture/proposals/graph-curation-surface.md` (data-flow, register DM-GQ-1..7, OQ-29, the "but what if" edge-case pass, affected components, S-slice boundaries) + two glossary terms (`reification`, `surrogate-key`). **Goal:** V1 — the ingest→graph→viewer PoC (M0–M4) — is **feature-complete** (the M4
multi-story live smoke PASSED, Session 54). Before the next *build* milestone, **lock the
portfolio presentation**: make the public repo something a stranger can land on and
understand — an honest spec, a compelling README with demo artifacts, navigable code docs,
and clean doc hygiene. **Planning / docs / spec milestone — little-to-no production code.**
Direction owner-DECIDED (Session 54): **Public-readiness → Graph-quality polish → V2
Editing** (`docs/PLAN_LONG.md` amended; M0–M4 ticked, the two new milestones inserted before
V2).

**Slicing — skeleton + first session detailed (owner's call, S55 roll); later sessions are
sliced finer when picked up (a branchy one gets a `meta-architect:decompose-requirement`
step-0 as its own first slice):**

   the story didn't live. The doc tells, for an outsider: the **threat model first** (solo, local,
   single trusted user — *why* a local-DoS advisory is waivable), **supply chain** (14-day/7-day

   `npm audit`, the digest-pinned scanner), the **waiver lifecycle** (fix-first → scoped

- **2026-06-26 — Session 65: GitHub housekeeping + branch protection on `main` via a repository ruleset (governance/infra; ADR 0009 + doc updates in PR #155 `1722ea9`, the GitHub settings applied via API).** Three units in one conversation by explicit owner consent: (1) merged the **forgotten Session-64 close PR #154** (`6763ea6`) that `/resume-session` caught open; (2) **branch cleanup** — `git fetch --prune` cleared ~80 stale local remote-tracking refs (GitHub auto-deletes branches on merge) and 6 genuinely-leftover branches were deleted (each confirmed mapped to a MERGED PR), leaving only `main` local+remote; (3) the **S63 branch-protection-tighten** task. **Decision (owner chose "do it now" after an ADR-shaped discussion + web research):** replace the classic branch protection on `main` with a single **repository ruleset** (`main-protection`) — require a PR (0 approvals, squash-only, linear history), block force-push/deletion, require four status checks (`secret-scan`, `backend`, `frontend`, `security`); `ollama-cloud-smoke` left informational (external Ollama Cloud dependency); the sole admin is an **audited bypass actor** (escape hatch against self-lockout). Classic protection deleted so `main` has one governing mechanism. **Key technical finding (web-researched, not memory):** required status checks are safe because the code jobs skip via job-level `if:` (one `ci.yml`) and GitHub reports an `if:`-skipped job as **success** — so a docs PR is gated by `secret-scan` while a code PR must pass all four; **empirically confirmed** — PR #155 (docs-only, the first PR under the ruleset) went `MERGEABLE`/`CLEAN` with the code jobs skipping (the S56 runtime-verify-the-gate lesson). Rationale + alternatives in **[ADR 0009](decisions/0009-branch-protection-ruleset.md)**; `SECURITY_POSTURE.md` rewritten from "force-push/deletion only" to the ruleset. *Considered & rejected:* extending classic protection (rulesets are the modern, auditable, exportable mechanism); requiring `ollama-cloud-smoke` (couples merges to an external service); no bypass actor (self-lockout risk on a solo repo); requiring ≥1 approval (impossible solo); requiring the `changes` dispatcher to close a near-zero-probability "dispatcher fails → gates skip→pass" hole (the documented `ci-success` aggregator is the proper fix if it ever matters); a `pragma: allowlist secret` for a detect-secrets false positive on a dense plan line (reworded to defer the check-name list to the ADR instead — better prose). **Self-`/review-pr`** ready — docs verified claim-for-claim against the live ruleset, one low-risk observation accepted. **Retro:** `/retro` offered, owner **skipped** — the reflective pass found `/resume` caught the forgotten PR (its job), the ADR-shaped flow + web research worked, and the one friction (the detect-secrets false positive) was self-catching and reworded out; nothing cleared the bar for a rule/skill change. **Checks:** docs-only PR #155 — code gates n/a; CI docs-skip (`changes` + `secret-scan`) green + the ruleset's required checks satisfied; `main` clean post-merge.

- **2026-06-26 — Session 65: GitHub housekeeping + proper branch protection on `main` (governance/infra; PR #155 merged green, `1722ea9`; the ruleset applied via the GitHub API).** Cleared a small backlog of GitHub-side hygiene the owner sequenced deliberately, one step at a time. **(1)** Merged the **forgotten Session-64 close PR #154** — `/resume-session` caught it sitting open and unmerged, which is exactly its job; it edits `PLAN_SHORT.md`, so landing it first kept it from diverging against later plan edits. **(2) Branch cleanup:** `git fetch --prune` cleared ~80 stale *local remote-tracking* refs (GitHub already auto-deletes branches on merge — the local copy just hadn't pruned); the 6 genuinely-leftover branches were each confirmed mapped to a MERGED PR and deleted, leaving only `main` on the remote and locally. **(3) Branch protection done properly** (the S63 follow-up): after an ADR-shaped discussion (the owner flagged it as such) and web research into the GitHub required-status-checks footgun, the classic protection was replaced with a **repository ruleset** (`main-protection`) — a PR is required (squash-only, linear history, 0 approvals, since a solo maintainer can't approve their own PR), force-push/deletion blocked, four status checks required (`secret-scan` + the three code jobs; `ollama-cloud-smoke` left informational as an external-dependency check). The sole admin is an audited bypass actor. Classic protection was removed so `main` has one governing mechanism. ADR 0009 records the rationale + alternatives; `SECURITY_POSTURE.md`'s branch-protection section was rewritten to match. **The footgun avoided:** a required check that never *runs* blocks the merge forever — but only when a whole workflow is skipped by a path filter; our jobs skip via job-level `if:`, which GitHub counts as success, so docs PRs aren't wedged. **Confirmed empirically** — PR #155 (the first PR under the ruleset, docs-only) went `MERGEABLE`/`CLEAN` with the code jobs skipping (the S56 "runtime-verify a CI-gating change" lesson applied). A `detect-secrets` false positive on a dense plan line was reworded out (deferring the check-name list to the ADR) rather than suppressed with a pragma. **Lesson:** branch protection that requires status checks is only safe to turn on once you've confirmed *how* your CI skips — job-level `if:` skips count as success (safe to require), workflow-level path-filter skips hang as pending (would wedge the merge); the distinction is the whole decision, and it's verifiable in one real PR. **`/retro` offered, owner skipped** (no friction cleared the bar). **Next: the PoC→next-phase preparation gate** — review the PoC spec, author a Graph-quality milestone spec, review `PLAN_LONG`, adjust the `AGENTS.md`/`CLAUDE.md` set, consider new skills; the **milestone roll** + the **S61 plan-trim learning-loop prep** remain pending and entangled with it (the prep gate naturally precedes the roll). **Checks:** docs-only PR #155 — code CI gates n/a; CI docs-skip (`changes` + `secret-scan`) green + the ruleset's required checks satisfied; `main` clean post-merge. Three units in one conversation by explicit owner consent.

The Demo section was written to stand on its own on the bundled Oakhaven sample, so no `TODO` or broken image embed lands on `main` between this slice and the screenshot-capture slice (B). **The session's real lesson came from the owner's review:** the README — faithfully drawn from spec §2.1 — claimed Story Forge is "a genuine personal tool for an author writing *Wody Święte*", and the owner flagged that this is not true: the sample stories are LLM-generated for the PoC, there is no real manuscript, and personal authoring/research use is only a longer-term aim. This was a *foundational-input* overclaim, not as-built drift — it had propagated from the spec/interview into the README and the vault, and Session 58's vault re-sync (a freshness/honesty sweep just one session earlier) could not have caught it, because no internal consistency check can know the owner isn't the persona the spec assumes. The public-readiness "stranger reads it cold" lens is exactly what surfaced it. Ran the stop-and-amend (owner: "amend now"): spec §2.1 reframed (Wody Święte as the project's test fixture), vault `PROJECT.md`/`overview.md` reconciled, the README made honest. Also opened a 6th milestone session (Security & CI posture writeup) at the resume scope review, since the CVE/CI story lived only in internal records. **Retro** produced two vault-convention edits: a *hand-edit-vs-route-to-sweep* rule in `architecture/AGENTS.md`, and a new §1b *"foundational inputs the sweep can't verify"* in the `review-architecture` skill — the latter naming the structural reason Session 58's honesty sweep couldn't have caught the overclaim (a wrong owner-asserted premise reads as consistent everywhere). **Next: Public-readiness Session 3 Slice B** (screenshot capture) — or Session 4 (code docs), owner's pick. **Checks:** docs-only — code CI gates don't apply; CI ran the docs-skip green; self-`/review-pr` clean.
- **2026-06-25 — Session 58 (Public-readiness Session 2): the architecture-vault re-sync + a retro fix to the sweep skill (vault/skill docs only; PR #140 merged green, `842bd54`).** Ran `meta-architect:review-architecture` at the V1 → Public-readiness roll to bring the vault — part of what a stranger reads — current with reality. The report (`architecture/reports/2026-06-25-architecture-review.md`) found **no blockers** and two risks, both vault drift fixed on sight: the vault still framed the spaCy PreNER baseline as a *live pipeline stage* though spec §7 Step 3 was just amended to deferred/dormant (Session 57) — reconciled `PROJECT.md`/`overview.md` after **verifying against the code** that PreNER is genuinely dormant (the live `/extract` passes empty hints, the coordinator has no PreNER call); and `overview.md`'s as-built snapshot had stopped at M4.S3a though S3b/S3c/multi-story all shipped and V1 is feature-complete (the 4th recurrence of doc-freshness drift) — refreshed, with the world graph reframed as post-PoC. `invariants.md` was code-verified honest (INV-9's six writer-paths confirmed against `neo4j_repo.py`/`entity_edit.py`; the coordinator constructs no graph writer) and its lagging frontmatter date bumped; a BUILT banner was added to `m4-multi-story`; the forward "but what if" (auto-chunker silent content-loss; membership-derivation under delete) was homed as OQ-28 for the coming Graph-quality milestone. - **2026-06-25 — Session 57 (Public-readiness Session 1): the PreNER spec↔reality stop-and-amend (spec/docs only; PR #138 merged green, `d0ee135`).** The spec had described the spaCy `PreNERAgent` as an active pre-LLM pipeline stage (§7 "Step 3: Pre-NER baseline"; the §7 Step-4 optimization note), but in code it is dormant — built yet wired into nothing, so the live extraction path is LLM-only. The architecture vault still frames PreNER as a live stage but is writer-restricted (ADR 0002), so it was left for the next session's architecture sweep to reconcile rather than hand-edited. Self-review was clean (the load-bearing check was the whole-repo decision-reconciliation grep); CI exercised the new docs-skip cadence correctly (only the change-detector and secret-scan ran, the heavy suites skipped). **Lesson:** the handoff had loosely cited the drift as "§6 / §3" when the pipeline actually lives in **§7** — resume caught it by grepping rather than trusting the label, and the amend now records the correct section everywhere, fixing the imprecision at its source. **Next: Public-readiness Session 2** — the architecture-vault re-sync (`meta-architect:review-architecture`). **Checks:** docs/spec-only — code CI gates don't apply.
- **2026-06-25 — Session 56: unplanned interrupt — repo went PUBLIC + CI rework + light branch protection + stale-branch cleanup (PR #135, merged green; infra + a §6.7 spec amendment, no product code).** GitHub Actions stopped mid-session — the **private** repo's free-minutes pool was exhausted. Root cause: the repo was private though "public from day one" is baked into the spec/`AGENTS.md`; flipped it to **public** after a clean git-history pre-flight (no `.env`/secrets/keys ever committed) → unlimited free standard-runner Actions, unblocked. **CI restructure (`ci.yml`):** a native `changes` job (git-diff, no new action) path-scopes the heavy jobs (service-container suites, frontend build, dep-age/OSV/Trivy scans) to **code-bearing** changes (outside `docs/**`, `architecture/**`, `*.md`); `detect-secrets` split into an **always-on `secret-scan`**; a **daily `schedule`** force-runs the scans so the CVE-treadmill is caught regardless of PR cadence; `concurrency` cancels superseded PR runs; uv/npm caching. **§6.7 stop-and-amend** (the docs-skip touches the stated "scans on every push/PR" rule): added a "CI scan cadence" bullet, adjusted the OSV/Trivy cadence lines + the §7 CI list, reconciled `AGENTS.md` merge-flow + the `pin-image` skill — framed *adapts-not-relaxes* (every code change still fully scanned + a daily run). **Light branch protection** on `main` (block force-push/delete + require a PR; no required reviews/checks — owner keeps the merge button). **Stale-branch cleanup** — deleted 8 leftover remote branches (all merged PRs). **Verified the docs-skip empirically** on a throwaway scratch PR (#136, closed): a docs-only diff ran only `changes` + `secret-scan`; the 4 heavy jobs skipped. **Self-`/review-pr` clean** — the dangerous misclassification direction (a code file scored as docs → scans skipped on real code) is structurally impossible: the regex only matches `*.md`/`docs/**`/`architecture/**`. **Retro:** tightened `wrap-session` step 8 to say a docs PR now runs only the secret-scan (and branch protection requires the PR). **Lesson:** runtime-verify a CI gating change on a scratch branch rather than reasoning about the skipped path — cheap certainty. **Checks:** PR #135 merged green (full suite — it edits `.github/**` = code-bearing); main post-merge CI green. **Next: Public-readiness Session 1** — the PreNER spec↔reality stop-and-amend (unchanged; this was an interrupt).

**Completed-milestone task section (M4).**

## Completed milestone: Milestone 4 — V1 polish

_Retained as history — M4 ("V1 polish") is **feature-complete**: inline highlights, the entity side panel, manual correction in the reader (edit · merge/delete/undo · tag/un-tag/boundaries), and narrowed multi-story (per-story membership + the §3.4 this-story/whole-project scope toggle) all shipped and live-smoke-verified (Session 54). The world-graph parent was cut from PoC (S44). M4 completed all of V1 (the ingest→graph→viewer PoC, M0–M4)._

**Goal (spec §9 M4 / `docs/PLAN_LONG.md`):** the "V1 polish" set — **inline highlights**, side
panel, manual annotation, properties/relations edit, **multi-story**, ~~world-graph parent~~ — that turns
the working ingest→graph pipeline into a usable V1 authoring surface. **Scope narrowed 2026-06-22 (owner,
Decided S44): the world-graph parent (cross-story world merge, §3.6) is OUT of PoC → `docs/BACKLOG.md`;
multi-story narrows to "add a new story that reuses the project graph + per-story entity membership"
(no cross-story merge). The spec §3.6/§9 still describe the world graph — reconciling them is a pending
stop-and-amend before the multi-story slice.** Two seams M3 deferred **graduate
to live M4 work**: the **§3.4 graph story-vs-project scoping** (multi-story breaks the one-story-per-
project assumption the graph route rests on) and **DM-Rel-5**'s written-edge re-point (an
accepted-entity↔entity merge, first possible in M4, re-points an already-written edge). INV-2's
consent gate stays **deferred past M3** (persona-justified).

**First slice — M4.S1 inline highlights** (owner-chosen, 2026-06-17 roll). Decomposed step-0:
`architecture/proposals/m4-inline-highlights.md` (register **OPEN — DM-IH-1..8 / OQ-21**). A
**read-only projection** of the accepted graph (spec §3.5): render the story text, highlight accepted
entities inline (colour-by-type), hover→tooltip. **Centre of gravity = DM-IH-1 span resolution** —
`entity_mentions` carry **null char offsets**, so highlighting is a *where-does-this-entity-sit* problem
(render-time string search vs persisting real spans vs hybrid; PL inflection is the headline gap).
Side-panel, manual annotation, properties/relations edit, multi-story, ~~world graph~~ (cut S44) are **later** slices.

**Feature order** (sliced at the 2026-06-17 roll; later slices sequenced as decomposed):

1. **M4.S1 — inline highlights** (read-only reader + accepted-entity highlights + hover tooltip; spec §3.5).
   ✅ **DONE — backend (Session 32, PR #81) + frontend (Session 33, PR #86), live-verified.** Register
   resolved with the owner — DM-IH-1 (render-time search over name+aliases, *verify-first*: no stored
   span exists to persist), DM-IH-2 (new `GET /stories/{id}/reader`), DM-IH-3 (plain `<mark>` renderer,
   not Tiptap), DM-IH-4 (longest-match), DM-IH-7 (accepted-only), DM-IH-8 (name+type+aliases), DM-IH-5
   (reader-local fixed palette + hash fallback + legend, owner's call S33), DM-IH-6 (whole-story render;
   measured fine on the Oakhaven draft). Frontend = `features/text-reader/` (pure splitter + palette +
   `useReader` hook + `<mark>` renderer + tooltip + legend + route + graph link), test-first; both review
   passes ran. **Verified end-to-end by the Session-33 Oakhaven smoke test** (upload → chunk → extract →
   review/dedup → relations → reader), which surfaced ~12 post-PoC items now in `docs/BACKLOG.md`.
   _Next: side panel → manual annotation → properties/relations edit (incl. the DM-Rel-5 written-edge
   re-point) → multi-story + §3.4 scoping → ~~world graph~~ (cut S44). The smoke test argued for prioritising
   manual correction in the reader (it's where errors surface) — confirm slice order at resume._

   "local graph around that entity"). **Owner-chosen 2026-06-18 (Session 34)** over manual-correction-
   in-reader — the read-only inspection surface the next slice's corrections build on. Decomposed
   step-0: `architecture/proposals/m4-side-panel.md` (register **DM-SP-1..8 resolved / OQ-22**). Click a
   highlighted entity → side panel with its details (canonical/aliases/type/**properties**/occurrences/
   relations/timeline) + a **1-hop [[ego-graph]]** mini-view. **Centre of gravity = DM-SP-1 data
   source → a focused per-entity endpoint** `GET /stories/{id}/entities/{eid}` (BFF: server-side
   cross-store join + the 1-hop neighbourhood + occurrences; needs a new `Neo4jRepo` 1-hop query),
   which **splits the slice** (DM-SP-7):
   - **M4.S2a — backend** ✅ **DONE (PR #89, 2026-06-18, Session 34).** `domain/neighbourhood.py`
     (pure `build_ego_graph`) + `Neo4jRepo.get_neighbourhood` (1-hop, project-scoped) +

   Read-only this slice (INV-1/3/9 untouched); property/relation **editing**, manual tagging, "not this

3. **M4.S3a — the side panel becomes editable** (the **first M4 *write* slice**; spec §3.4 "properties
   editable"/"relations editable" + §3.5 manual correction). Edit an accepted entity's

   resolved). **The first slice that *writes* committed graph state** — the design weight is the write
   path + reversibility, not the UI: **DM-S3a-1 = new named edit handlers + reword INV-9** ("exactly two

   precedent, **ADR drafted at build, test-first**); **DM-S3a-2 = a before→after edit-evidence log**
   (INV-3 undo + flywheel); **DM-S3a-3** route manual relation-adds through the existing decide path

   **DM-S3a-5** typed `properties` values (keys free, INV-4); **DM-S3a-7 = split** S3a-be / S3a-fe.
   - **M4.S3a-be — backend** ✅ **DONE (PR #96, 2026-06-19, Session 37).** `domain/entity_edits.py`

     regenerated. **INV-9 reworded + `docs/decisions/0006` (broaden-don't-mint)** landed; relation/
     candidate state-machine notes extended. **DM-S3a-3 resolved-at-build to a *direct* edge-writer**
     (option b): the decide path resolves endpoints by surface-name-within-a-paragraph, which a
     hand-picked edge lacks, so routing through it doesn't compose — owner-approved the pre-authorized
     fallback; INV-9's edge-writer set grows too. Both review gates ran (`/review-pr` caught a
     blank-predicate 500→422; `/code-review` caught a predicate whitespace-strip).
   - **M4.S3a-fe — frontend** ✅ **DONE (PR #98, 2026-06-20, Session 38).** `useEntityEdit`/`useAddRelation`/
     `useRemoveRelation` mutation hooks (+ `patchJsonBody`/204-safe `del` client helpers) with
     reader+graph+entity-detail invalidation (DM-S3a-4); a pure `propertiesEditor.ts` (typed scalar rows,
     nested/array values preserved as read-only JSON — DM-S3a-5/INV-4); `ReaderEntityPanel` gained an Edit
     mode (name/type/aliases/properties) + a relations add (reusing `EntityPicker`)/remove section with the
     `merged_into_existing` warning. **One small read-side backend add** (the lone deviation from "no backend
     change"): `language` on `EntityDetailResponse`, so the single name field writes the project-language
     `canonical_name_{pl,en}` slot — **bilingual-per-project is out of PoC scope** (spec §10 q8, owner). Both
     review gates ran; live-smoke-verified. Live smoke surfaced a UX nit (relation-direction toggle), folded.
   _Then: **S3b** merge/delete/undo (DM-Rel-5 re-point) → S3c tag/boundaries/spans → multi-story + §3.4
   scoping → ~~world graph~~ (cut S44)._

4. **M4.S3b — graph mutations that need downstream cleanup (merge · delete · undo).** The slice S3a named
   at its seam, and the **first to re-point already-written graph state**. **Scope + decompose ✅ DONE
   (Session 39, 2026-06-20); register RESOLVED.** Step-0 → `architecture/proposals/m4-s3b-graph-mutations.md`
   (`accepted`, register **DM-S3b-1..8 / OQ-25** resolved). Owner calls: **general undo** (any edit/merge/
   delete reversible newest-first via a grouped append-only `graph_edits` log — a *compensating transaction*;
   resolves spec §10 q2) **+ undo must *show what it reverses*** (each operation carries a human-readable
   description; preview + confirm); **merge = author picks survivor, resolves property conflicts by hand**
   (owner chose more control over survivor-wins); **real `DETACH DELETE` + full-snapshot undo** (not soft).
   INV-3 goes from *substrate* (S3a recorded) to *executed* (undo); INV-9 enumeration unchanged (ops live in
   `EntityEditService`); **split be/fe taken — and the be1(merge)/be2(delete+undo) cut taken too** (owner-
   chosen, Session 40); **ADR 0007** at build. **Spec amended (Session 39):** §3.4 (merge + delete in the
   detail panel) + §10 q2 (undo).
   - **M4.S3b-be1 — backend (merge)** ✅ **DONE (PR #102, 2026-06-20, Session 40).** The first operation to
     re-point already-committed identity: merge B into survivor A — pure `domain/entity_merge.py`
     (`plan_merge`/`detect_property_conflicts`: alias union, by-hand conflict resolution, content-addressed
     edge repoint/fold/self-loop) → `graph_edits` **grouping migration** (`operation_id`/`seq`/`op_kind`/
     `description`/`project_id`/`undone_at`) + `PostgresEditStore.record_operation` → `Neo4jRepo.delete_entity`
     + `repoint_entity_mentions` (RETURNING moved ids) → `EntityEditService.merge_entities` (**B deleted last
     so a crashed merge stays retryable** — the `/code-review` fold) → `POST …/entities/{eid}/merge`
     (400/404/409/503; OpenAPI + client regen). **ADR 0007** landed (merge/delete/undo contract + grouped-log-
     as-undo-substrate + write order); INV-9 grep guard widened (+`delete_entity`, fourth-instance); INV-3
     grouped-log note (substrate now, executed in be2); relation/candidate lifecycle notes extended. Both
     review gates ran; `/review-pr` folded two (incident-edge dedup, resolved-properties restriction),
     `/code-review` folded the write-order retryability fix. 427 backend tests green.
   - **M4.S3b-be2 — backend (delete + undo)** ✅ **DONE (PR #105, 2026-06-20, Session 42).** Whole-entity
     **delete** (real `DETACH DELETE` + full-snapshot before-image) + the general **undo executor**
     (`POST …/graph-edits/undo`, undo-last, preview + confirm): `PostgresEditStore.latest_live_operation`
     (COALESCE `operation_id`→`id`) / `mark_operation_undone` read path → pure `domain/graph_undo.invert_operation`
     → `EntityEditService.delete_entity` + `undo_last` (drift-check → 409, reverse-`seq` replay) → the two
     endpoints. INV-3 *executed*; `state-machines/graph-operation.md` (`applied → undone`) drawn; INV-9 fifth
     witnessed instance (undo reverses via the same human-reached writers). **Re-do-after-undo id collision
     resolved = a generation discriminator** (a `uuid5` seed suffix past any *undone* op for the same targets;
     retry-stable because a *live* op probes False) — kept the `undone_at` stamp model rather than the ADR's
     delete-the-rows alternative; applies to re-merge *and* re-delete. **DM-S3b-5 confirmed (owner, S42): allow
     the delete + let the merge's undo drift-check refuse** (no survivor-guard on delete). Both review gates ran;
     **`/code-review` caught a real data-loss bug** (`fold_relation` undo deleted A's pre-existing edge) — folded
     + two sibling undo-correctness fixes (folded-add no-op, remove-relation full-fidelity). Undo/delete
     **robustness hardening** (depth cap, single-`created_at`-per-op, neighbour-churn signal, row-factory dedup)
     → `docs/BACKLOG.md`.
   - **M4.S3b-fe — frontend** ✅ **DONE (PR #107, 2026-06-22, Session 43) — M4.S3b COMPLETE.** Reader/side-
     panel UI over the three merged routes, test-first (pure mapper → hook → component): `mergeConflicts.ts`
     (client-side conflict detection mirroring `detect_property_conflicts` — the merge 400 carries only key
     names, no values, so the by-hand resolver computes conflicts from both entities' `properties`);
     `useMergeEntities`/`useDeleteEntity`/`useUndo` (undo invalidates only on a *real* apply, not a preview);
     `MergeControls` (EntityPicker → conflict resolver → confirm → summary counts; self-merge blocked);
     delete-with-confirm in `ReaderEntityPanel`; `UndoButton` in the reader header (undo is *story*-scoped —
     owner call) with preview→confirm→apply + 404/409 handling. Both review gates clean; self-review nits
     folded (shared `formatPropertyValue`, reset-summary-on-pick, full-width merge section). **Browser smoke
     surfaced a backend bug → PR #108** (merge-undo 500); merge/delete/undo verified live after that fix.
   _Then: **S3c** tag/un-tag/change-boundaries (next — see item 5) → narrowed multi-story (new story +
   project graph + per-story entity membership; §3.4 scoping). **World-graph multi-story dropped from PoC
   2026-06-22 → `docs/BACKLOG.md`** (see Decided S44)._

5. **M4.S3c — manual tag / un-tag / change-boundaries** (the **final** "manual correction in the reader"
   slice; spec §3.5). **Scope + decompose ✅ DONE (Session 44, 2026-06-22); register RESOLVED.** Owner chose
   it as the next slice to build (over the narrowed multi-story work). Step-0 →
   `architecture/proposals/m4-s3c-manual-tagging.md` (`accepted`, register **DM-S3c-1..9 / OQ-26** resolved).
   **Centre of gravity:** a rendered highlight is a render-time *search hit with no saved identity* (DM-IH-1),
   so a manual span (inflected form / pronoun / new entity) can't be re-found by search and un-tagging has no
   row to delete. **Owner resolutions:** **DM-S3c-1 = (B) overlay / "save only what you touch"** (keep
   render-time search for auto highlights; manual tags persist stored spans that overlay+win; a rejected
   highlight writes a suppression the resolver subtracts; change-boundaries materializes one occurrence —
   incremental, no backfill, DM-IH-1's properties preserved); **DM-S3c-2 = both attach-existing +
   create-new-entity** (a new human-reached graph writer — INV-9 grows); **DM-S3c-7 = adopt Tiptap now**
   (owner override of my native-selection lean — V2 §4 editing inherits it; `/add-dependency` at fe build);
   tag/un-tag/boundary ride the S3b `graph_edits` undo (DM-S3c-5); add `source`+`mention_id` to
   `ReaderHighlight` (DM-S3c-6); **split be/fe** (DM-S3c-8); **no §3.5 capability amendment** (S3a
   precedent) — storage model + INV-9 reword in **ADR 0008** at build, a small **§6.4 data-model note** via
   stop-and-amend if the migration needs it. Completeness sweep over mention CRUD + entity-from-tag
   **closes** (no slicing gap; general split + relation qualifiers stay post-PoC).
   - **M4.S3c-be — backend** ✅ **DONE (PR #111, 2026-06-22, Session 45).** `domain/highlights.reconcile_highlights`
     (pure `search ∪ manual − suppressions`, manual-wins-then-longest-match, suppressions subtracted
     post-overlay; `Highlight` gains `source`+`mention_id` — `resolve_highlights` unchanged) +
     `entity_mentions.source` & a `mention_suppressions` table (migration `d5971b7919ab`, **§6.4 amended** via
     stop-and-amend — no §3.5 change) + five `EntityEditService` ops (tag-existing/tag-new/suppress/retag/
     change-boundaries) + four new undo op-kinds with inverters **contract-tested from the writer's real rows**
     (PR-#108 discipline) + routes `POST …/paragraphs/{pid}/{tags,suppressions,boundaries}` + the reconciled
     reader, test-first (523 backend + 247 frontend tests green); OpenAPI snapshot + typed client regenerated.
     **ADR 0008** landed + INV-9 reconciled (invariants.md sixth instance). Build refinement (ADR 0008 §4):
     rejection ("not an entity"/"not this entity") is **uniformly a suppression** (resolver clears it
     post-overlay, even over a manual span) — one mechanism, one inverse. Both review gates ran; `/code-review`
     folded one cleanup (`_mention_id` helper — dedup the id formula). DM-S3c-2 (tag-new) confirmed at build:
     `tag_new_entity` reaches the existing `create_entity` writer from the tag endpoint (no new graph symbol).
   - **M4.S3c-fe — frontend.** Split into two sessions (owner-chosen at the S47 plan, sizing the engine
     swap apart from the correction UI):
     - **M4.S3c-fe1 — Tiptap read-only migration** ✅ **DONE (PR #115, 2026-06-22, Session 47).** Replaced the
       per-paragraph `<mark>` renderer with one read-only **Tiptap editor + ProseMirror decorations** at
       behavioural parity (colour-by-type, tooltip, click + Enter/Space → side panel, occurrence flash); no
       write paths. Pure test-first modules `readerDoc` (paragraphs → doc, `paragraphId` per node) +
       `decorations` (codepoint→UTF-16 offset conversion against the original text — the verify-at-build, with
       an astral test — + decoration attrs); `ReaderEditor` is the isolated ProseMirror mount (no unit test,
       mocked in `TextReader.test`, browser-smoke-verified). Removed `ParagraphText` + `segments`. Dep:
       `@tiptap/*==3.26.0` (newest 3.x clearing the §6.7 soak, OSV-clean). Both review gates folded; browser
       parity smoke passed (it caught the read-only `handleKeyDown` gotcha — see Decided).
     - **M4.S3c-fe2 — the correction UI** ✅ **DONE (PR #117, 2026-06-22, Session 48).** Built on the fe1
       editor: pure `selectionOffsets.ts` (UTF-16 selection → codepoint span, inverse of
       `codepointToUtf16`); the **right-click context menu** (`ReaderContextMenu` — tag-as-entity on a
       selection; not-this-entity / re-assign / not-an-entity / change-boundaries on a highlight); the
       **`ReaderCorrectionPopover`** (reuse `EntityPicker` for tag-existing/re-assign + a new-entity form,
       open-world type); the three **mutation hooks** (`useTagOccurrence`/`useSuppressOccurrence`/
       `useChangeBoundaries`) invalidating reader/detail/graph; `decorations` emit
       `data-source`/`data-mention-id`/`data-start`/`data-end` so a right-click addresses the exact
       occurrence; `ReaderEditor` gained the selection-capture adapter (PM selection primary, native DOM
       fallback — the lone untestable surface, browser-smoke-verified). Change-boundaries = **re-select +
       confirm** (owner-chosen UX). Undo reuses `UndoButton`. ADR 0008 §4: both rejections POST a
       *suppression*, never a delete. No backend/schema change. 285 frontend tests (+39); both review gates
       folded; owner browser smoke confirmed all flows. **"Manual correction in the reader" is now
       feature-complete (S3a edit · S3b merge/delete/undo · S3c tag/un-tag/boundaries).**
   _Then: narrowed multi-story (new story + project graph + per-story entity membership; needs its own
   decompose + a §3.6/§9 stop-and-amend) → V1 polish wrap._
