**Milestone-4 Decided entries** (reverse-chronological, verbatim).

- **2026-06-24 — Session 54: M4 multi-story LIVE SMOKE = PASS → M4 feature-complete; dev-data workaround for a silently-truncated story; 10 graph-quality findings harvested (no production code).** The end-to-end verification of the shipped multi-story feature (S51+S52+S53). **Method:** stack already up; migrated the dev DB (it was behind at `d5971b7919ab` → head `c0c7904a555c`); drove the **API surface** (no browser-automation tool in this env) while the owner drove the browser UI. **Verified:** `GET /projects` picker data; **add-story-into-project** (oakhaven-2 → Oakhaven, `story_count` 1→2); **cross-story dedup** (oakhaven-2's candidates matched against oakhaven's accepted graph — 56 merge proposals → 24 distinct story-1 entities); the **§3.4 scope toggle** filtering both **nodes and edges** correctly (`scope=story` 88n/93e ⊂ `scope=project` 176n/228e, identical from either story) — owner confirmed the toggle live. **Workaround decision (dev data):** the auto-chunker had **silently truncated oakhaven-2** — its LLM outline dropped all of Chapter Six's content (kept only the header), so the reader showed 19 paragraphs and extraction never saw the storm/boarding scenes. Because the system has **no re-structure (409) and no delete-story** (both deferred features), and a full manual re-structure would orphan the already-confirmed entities' mention-links (breaking `scope=story` until a full re-extract+re-review), the owner chose to **preserve the confirmed work**: a targeted DB insert of the 6 missing Chapter-Six paragraphs (text pulled via the real `parse_manual_outline`, dry-run-verified, 6 `INSERT`s only — nothing deleted) + a **resume-extract** that processed *only* those 6 paragraphs (the per-paragraph checkpoint skipped the 19 done) → a small Ch6 candidate batch the owner reviewed. Result: complete story (25 paragraphs), all prior confirmations intact, Ch6 entities/relations in the graph. *Considered & rejected:* a clean manual re-structure (correct structure but loses all the review effort — the thing the owner explicitly wanted to keep); leaving it truncated (owner wanted the complete story). **Findings → `docs/BACKLOG.md` (10) + a cross-cutting spec-drift (1):** auto-chunk no-retry-on-overflow **and** the more serious **silent content-drop / no coverage check** (`manual` is the only trustworthy structuring mode until fixed); a "New entity" card with an armed (amber) merge target reads as if Accept will merge; merge candidates show only name+score (can't verify *which* entity — sharpened by the score-100 "crew" false-merge, two different ships' crews); the relation card shows **no source context** (can't commit a relation blindly); modality/irrealis, n-ary arity, and eventive-vs-stative + timeline-ordering as relation-modelling gaps; predicate proliferation (semantic relation merge); the graph view as a direct editing/curation surface; and the **spaCy PreNER spec drift** (§6 step 3 / §3 step 4 describe PreNER as an active pipeline stage, but it's dormant — the live `/extract` is LLM-only) → routed to cross-cutting as a stop-and-amend, with the spaCy-without-LLM eval captured in backlog. **Retro:** reflective pass run — nothing cleared the bar for a skill/rule change; owner concluded the session (skip `/retro`). **Roadmap direction DECIDED this session (owner):** M4 done = all of V1/PoC complete; the next-phase sequence is **Public-readiness/docs → Graph-quality polish → V2 Editing → V3 Style** (`docs/PLAN_LONG.md` amended — M2/M3/M4 ticked, the two new milestones inserted before V2). The **Public-readiness pass is next** (README + demo artifacts + code docs + the two spec↔reality reconciliations [PreNER dormant, world graph cut] + doc hygiene — lock the portfolio presentation before the next build); then a **Graph-quality milestone that opens with a backlog-triage conversation** (the 10 Session-54 findings) to make the graph trustworthy before writing features. **The mechanical roll execution** (byte-exact archive move of M4 → `PLAN_ARCHIVE.md` + scaffolding the Public-readiness task list) is the next session's first task — deferred from this long conversation, kept light. *Considered & rejected:* jumping straight to V2 (build writing on an untrustworthy graph); doing the graph-quality work first (a stranger should land on a legible repo before we polish internals). **Checks:** docs-only session (`docs/BACKLOG.md` + `docs/PLAN_SHORT.md` + `docs/PLAN_LONG.md`) — code gates n/a; the *running app* was the verification.
- **2026-06-24 — Session 53: M4 multi-story FRONTEND slice shipped (PR #130) + oakhaven-2 sample (PR #131).** Built the §3.4 reader/graph experience over the S52 backend, **test-first**, consuming the existing typed-client surface (no backend/generated-client change). **Owner scope call (resume):** include the **add-story-into-project** path, not a read-only picker+toggle — so multi-story is reachable and demonstrable end-to-end through the UI. *Considered & rejected:* read-only picker + toggle only (the scope toggle would have nothing to toggle without a UI way to put a 2nd story in a project). **Design choices:** (a) `useStoryGraph` carries `scope` as the **3rd query-key element** (`["story-graph", storyId, scope]`) so the existing 28 prefix-invalidation callers (`storyGraphQueryKey(storyId)`) still refetch both scopes and a flip repaints from cache — no caller churn (*rejected:* changing the shared key signature); (b) the add-to-project target rides the **URL** (`?project_id=&project_name=`), not router `location.state` — a `/code-review` finding (state evaporates on reload → silent new-project); (c) on upload success, **invalidate the project + project-stories caches** keyed off the response `project_id` (a `/code-review` finding — was stale 30 s); (d) the graph scope toggle **resets the node selection** (a `/code-review` finding — a node picked project-wide blanked the panel when narrowing). **The dual review gate paid off (the PR-#36 pattern again):** `/review-pr` (self) declared clean; `/code-review` (high, 8 finders) caught those **3 real bugs** + the 30 s-stale list + the panel blank — all folded with tests. **Deferred (owner-approved):** cross-story project-scope graph-cache coherence — a graph edit invalidates only the edited story's prefix, leaving a *sibling* story's project-scoped view stale for 30 s; self-healing, no data risk, the fix touches ~11 unrelated mutation hooks → `docs/BACKLOG.md`. **The oakhaven-2 sample** (a continuation of `oakhaven.md`, Chapters 4–5, with deliberate coreference cases) shipped as its own docs-only PR (#131), split out per "don't scope-creep". *Considered & rejected:* folding the sample into the FE PR (unrelated). **Checks:** 306 frontend tests green (was 285); build + lint clean; all 4 CI jobs green on both PRs; owner gave the per-merge OK on each.
- **2026-06-24 — Session 52: M4 multi-story BACKEND slice shipped (PR #128).** Built the resolved register (DM-MS-1..4) **test-first**, no new decompose: story-scoped graph read (`scope=story|project` on `GET /stories/{id}/graph`, **default `story`**) via a pure `domain/story_scope.filter_graph_to_story` fed by derived membership; optional `project_id` on upload (404 on a dangling project — fail-closed); `GET /projects` (+ derived `story_count`) and `GET /projects/{id}/stories`. **No new migration, no new dependency** (membership is *derived*, DM-MS-1). Shared `ErrorResponse` extracted to `api/responses.py`; OpenAPI snapshot + typed client regenerated. **Edge-rule refinement (owner call, this session):** a hand-added relation carries no `source_paragraph_id`, which the resolved DM-MS-2 rule didn't consider; owner chose **null-source edges are story-agnostic** — shown in `scope=story` whenever both endpoints are story-members. This preserves DM-MS-2's "`scope=story` is a no-op for single-story projects" guarantee (the literal rule would have hidden manual edges). *Considered & rejected:* applying the literal rule (would drop manual edges from single-story views). **Review:** `/review-pr` clean; `/code-review` (high, 8-angle) found no bugs and one efficiency fold — `scope=story` was loading 768-dim mention embeddings just for `entity_id`, so added a lean id-only `list_entity_ids_for_story` (commit `4966368`). 543 backend + 285 frontend tests green; all CI jobs green. Frontend picker + §3.4 toggle is the next slice (separate PR).
- **2026-06-24 — Session 51: M4 multi-story OPENER (`world_id` cleanup) shipped + a security-treadmill waiver.** Built the resolved-register's low-risk opener (DM-MS-5) **test-first**: dropped the always-null `projects.world_id` and its plumbing (migration `c0c7904a555c` + 6 code homes + the §3.3 code-mirror reword + regen). The register was already RESOLVED (S50), so no new design decision — a clean execution slice (PR #124). *Considered & rejected:* chaining straight into the multi-story backend slice — paused at the PR boundary (the Session-50 one-unit-per-conversation rule), owner directed each next step. **Security:** a HIGH bundled-jackson-databind pair (CVE-2026-54512/54513) reddened `main` overnight via the Trivy-DB treadmill (published 2026-06-23, unrelated to the docs PR that triggered the scan); **fix-first not possible** (jar vendored by neo4j, no soaked reship) → owner-approved scoped per-CVE waiver, condition-based drop-when (PR #126). pgvector + ollama confirmed clean by the full CI security run (a local ollama scan `exit=1` was a CUDA-lib **timeout**, not a finding — the lesson: a non-`--exit-code` Trivy `exit=1` is an *error*, not "vulns found").
- **2026-06-24 — GitHub Codex PR review retired.** The owner has no Codex subscription, so the GitHub-wired Codex PR review (the only residual external reviewer after Codex Desktop was retired 2026-06-10) no longer runs. Stripped its **forward-process** references from root `AGENTS.md` (§0 commit-hygiene note + the Merge-flow "Review model") and the `/review-pr` + `/wrap-session` skills; `/review-pr` (self) is now the sole standing review gate, with `/code-review` recommended for substantive code. **Kept intact:** all historical lesson citations ("Codex caught X in PR #Y" in `/review-pr`, the archive, CHANGELOG, vault reports, waiver notes) — they're the public record of *why* each review check exists. The standing question of whether `/code-review` becomes a *required* second gate is recorded as an open item in Blocked (deferred). *Considered & rejected:* erasing the historical Codex citations (would falsify the portfolio record — the project preserves history, it doesn't rewrite it).
- **2026-06-23 — Session 50 (M4 narrowed multi-story step-0 decompose + register RESOLVED + a tiny spec amendment; design/planning only — no production code).** The next M4 slice's full design pass; "manual correction in the reader" (S3a/S3b/S3c) is feature-complete. Step-0 → `architecture/proposals/m4-multi-story.md` (`accepted`, register **RESOLVED** DM-MS-1..7 / OQ-27). **The defining finding: the narrowed slice needs almost no new machinery.** Reading the as-built (3 Explore sweeps) showed (1) **per-story membership is already derivable** — `entity_mentions.paragraph_id → paragraphs → scenes → chapters → stories.id` is a real FK chain and the rollup query already exists (`postgres_repo.py:437-458` `list_entity_mentions_for_story()`); (2) the **matcher seed is already project-scoped** (`accepted_entity_reader.load_accepted(project_id)`), so a new story in an existing project auto-matches the project's known entities with **no cascade change** (the §B.4 incrementality test); (3) the **reader is already multi-story-correct** (project-scoped entities + story-scoped mentions). So the genuine gaps are only: create-story-**into-an-existing-project** (today every upload mints a new project), project/story **list** endpoints (none exist), and a **story-scoped graph read** for the §3.4 toggle. **Owner resolutions (one plain-language question at a time):** **DM-MS-1 = DERIVE membership from `entity_mentions`** (no new storage; single source of truth; edge membership via `source_paragraph_id`'s story — *rejected* a Neo4j property/edge and a membership table); **DM-MS-2 = a `scope=story|project` param on the existing `GET /stories/{id}/graph` route, DEFAULT `story`** — the owner **refined my `project` default → `story`** (safe because for single-story projects the two scopes return the identical graph, so the default flip is a no-op until a project gains a 2nd story; edge rule (i): show an edge only when both endpoints are story-members ∧ its source paragraph ∈ the story; *rejected* a new `/projects/{id}/graph` + re-pointed route); **DM-MS-3 = optional `project_id` on `POST /stories/upload`** (omitted ⇒ new project as today; "same upload, pick project first"); **DM-MS-4 = add `GET /projects` + `GET /projects/{id}/stories`** (read-only; implicit project creation kept, explicit `POST /projects` deferred); **DM-MS-5 = the `world_id` cleanup rides this slice + amend §8.4/§3.3 "whole world" → "whole project"**; **DM-MS-6 = verified already covered by M4.S3b** (the merge re-points incident edges — DM-Rel-5; multi-story adds no new merge trigger, nothing to build); **DM-MS-7 = split be/fe, backend one slice, the `world_id` cleanup the low-risk opener.** **No new invariant, no state machine, no ADR** (the slice is additive — DM-MS-1 *removes* a would-be data boundary by deriving). New glossary term `[[multi-tenancy]]` (project = the *tenancy key*, stored; a story = a *derived sub-scope*). **Spec amended this session (DM-MS-5, owner-approved):** §8.4 toggle + the §3.3 handpick-scope cross-reference, "whole world" → "whole project" (the S49 world-graph-out sweep keyed on "world graph" and missed these "whole world" phrasings — the "homes hide behind different words" lesson again; grep-verified no "whole world" remains in the spec). **New backlog item (owner side-note):** *dual-store data architecture* — revisit whether the Postgres+Neo4j split is optimal at PoC→V2 (`docs/BACKLOG.md`, ties OQ-1). *Considered & rejected:* storing membership (a second source of truth to sync); changing the existing graph-route semantics (DM-MS-2 b — a behaviour change for no PoC gain). **Checks:** docs/vault/spec only — no code, no deps; code gates n/a. **Next: build test-first** — the pure membership-rollup property → `world_id` cleanup (the opener) → `project_id`-on-upload + list endpoints + story-scoped read → OpenAPI/typed-client regen → then the frontend slice (picker + §3.4 toggle).

- **2026-06-22 — Session 48 (M4.S3c-fe2 built + merged, PR #117): the reader's manual-correction UI — "manual correction in the reader" is now feature-complete.** The fe write surface on top of the fe1 Tiptap editor (spec §3.5). **(1) The selection verify-at-build passed; the offset math is a pure tested module.** `selectionOffsets.selectionToSpan` maps a paragraph-relative **UTF-16** selection → **codepoint** span (the inverse of fe1's `codepointToUtf16`, via a new `utf16ToCodepoint`), rejecting empty/reversed client-side so a guaranteed-400 is never POSTed; astral + round-trip tested. **(2) The `editable:false`-constrains-selection risk (the S47 heads-up) was handled by a two-path adapter.** `ReaderEditor` resolves a selection via ProseMirror `editor.state.selection` first (gives a paragraph-relative `parentOffset` directly) and falls back to the native DOM `Selection` (walking the paragraph's text nodes) — the lone untestable surface, isolated + mocked in the container test, **browser-smoke-verified** (the owner confirmed selection + right-click both work read-only). **(3) Change-boundaries UX = re-select + confirm (owner-chosen)** over drag-handles / numeric inputs: pick the action → a banner → drag the new span → Confirm; reuses the one selection pipeline, no custom ProseMirror widget. A search hit materializes (no `mention_id`), a manual span edits in place (`mention_id` set). **(4) A right-click addresses the exact occurrence via DOM data-attrs** — `decorations` now emit `data-source`/`data-mention-id`/`data-start`/`data-end` (codepoints), the same pattern `handleClick` already uses for `data-entity-id`; no text selection needed for a highlight correction. **(5) Both rejections POST a suppression, never a delete (ADR 0008 §4)** — pinned in the hook + container tests. **(6) The three hooks invalidate reader+graph+entity-detail unconditionally** (the S3a rhythm) — cheap, avoids branching on whether a new entity was minted. **No backend or schema change** (routes + typed client already on `main`). **Reviews:** `/review-pr` clean; `/code-review` (high) refuted two correctness candidates (`data-start/end` always co-emitted with `data-entity-id`; the `""`-paragraphId URL is never constructed because `mutate` only fires while a phase is set) and folded one efficiency finding (gate the mouseup selection-resolve to boundary mode). **Owner smoke** found steps 2/4 (tag/re-assign to an existing entity) *working-as-designed* — the tagged form surfaces in the panel's **Occurrences** timeline (derived from highlights), not in aliases (DM-S3c-1 rejected alias-only) — and raised two post-PoC UX items (type hints; surface manual forms as aliases/known-forms), both recorded in `docs/BACKLOG.md`. *Considered & rejected:* a shared hook factory + a reusable toggle control + typed DOM-attr contract (`/code-review` candidates) — speculative abstraction inconsistent with the existing `useEntityEdit`/`handleClick` patterns (Karpathy). **Checks:** frontend 285 pass + lint/format/build clean; no deps changed; CI green on all four jobs; browser smoke confirmed all flows; owner gave the per-merge OK. `/retro` skipped (owner — the reflective pass found the rituals + the S47 handoff served the session well, nothing cleared the bar).
- **2026-06-22 — Session 47 (M4.S3c-fe1 built + merged, PR #115): reader migrated to Tiptap read-only + ProseMirror decorations.** Session A of a two-session split of M4.S3c-fe. **(1) Split the fe slice into fe1 (engine swap) + fe2 (correction UI), owner-chosen at the plan.** The full fe slice (a new dep + a render-layer rewrite + selection→offset + a right-click menu + tag picker + new-entity form + 3 mutation hooks) was too big for one reviewable session; fe1 reaches *behavioural parity* on Tiptap and lands the risky engine swap on its own, fe2 layers the write UI on top. The completeness sweep over the four correction operations confirmed they all home in fe2 — no slicing gap. *Considered & rejected:* one session/PR for the whole fe slice (a large diff across the render layer + 3 write paths, and a long stretch before a check-in). **(2) The verify-at-build was an offset-unit mismatch, handled by a pure tested module.** The backend emits highlight offsets as Python **codepoint** indices; ProseMirror counts **UTF-16** code units — they diverge by one per preceding astral character. `decorations.codepointToUtf16` converts against the *original paragraph text* (the same care `domain/highlights.py` takes), unit-tested with an emoji case; the same primitive inverts for fe2's selection→offset, so proving it here de-risks fe2. **(3) Minimal Tiptap extension set, no StarterKit** (Document + a custom Paragraph carrying `paragraphId` + Text) — the read-only reader needs no editing marks/history; fewer deps to pin. **(4) One whole-story editor, not per-paragraph** (my call, stated in the plan) — idiomatic, performant (DM-IH-6 measured whole-story render fine), and it gives fe2 a clean position→(paragraph, offset) mapping through the document model rather than the rendered DOM. **(5) The read-only `handleKeyDown` gotcha (caught by the browser smoke):** ProseMirror's `handleKeyDown` is an *edit* handler PM only runs while the view is editable, so on a read-only (`editable: false`) editor it never fires — Enter/Space-to-activate-a-highlight must be a React/DOM handler (a wrapper `onKeyDown` reading the focused span's `data-entity-id`), not a PM plugin prop. Click worked throughout because `handleClick` is a *regular* handler. **This is a live heads-up for fe2: `editable: false` also constrains text *selection* on a ProseMirror view — fe2's core mechanism — so selection handling there must not assume the default editable-view behaviour.** **Reviews:** `/review-pr` flagged the keyboard parity + an empty-doc `setContent` guard; `/code-review` (high, multi-angle) confirmed **zero correctness bugs** in the offset math/reactive sync and surfaced the tooltip-fallback parity + a `Flash`/`ReaderFlash` type dup + coverage gaps — **all folded**. `ReaderEditor` is an isolated untestable mount (no unit test, mocked in `TextReader.test`, browser-smoke-verified) — the same boundary as the cytoscape canvases. *Considered:* threading the highlighted surface text into the tooltip fallback (folded, for exact parity with the prior `<mark>`). **Checks:** frontend 246 pass + lint/format/build clean; dep-age green (`@tiptap/*==3.26.0`, 17 days old at pin, OSV-clean); CI green on all four jobs; browser parity smoke passed; owner gave the per-merge OK. `/retro` skipped (owner — the reflective pass found the browser-smoke-catches-what-jsdom-can't convention already fired as designed).

One rejection mechanism, one inverse (`RemoveSuppression`); honours DM-S3c-1(B)'s "a rejected highlight writes a suppression record." - **2026-06-22 — Session 44 (scope decisions + M4.S3c step-0 decompose).** Mid-session owner scope calls, before any S3c code. **(1) WORLD-LEVEL multi-story is OUT of PoC → `docs/BACKLOG.md`.** The "world graph" — a story belongs to a shared *world X* whose entities become cross-story merge candidates (spec §3.6; the world-graph-parent M4 slice) — is **dropped from the PoC**. This **concretizes** the long-deferred **§3.4 story-vs-project scoping** cross-cutting item (the data-model mechanism behind its "this story / whole world" toggle) — it is the in-PoC direction, *not* the dropped world-graph. The slice = the **final** "manual correction in the reader" slice (S3a · S3b · **S3c** tag/un-tag/change-boundaries; spec §3.5). **Centre of gravity:** today a rendered highlight is a render-time *search hit with no saved identity* (DM-IH-1; `entity_mentions` offsets are NULL/unused), so a manual span (an inflected form, a pronoun, a new entity) can't be re-found by search and un-tagging acts on a highlight with no row to delete. **Owner resolutions:** **DM-S3c-1 = (B) overlay / "save only what you touch"** — keep render-time search for auto highlights; a manual tag persists a **stored span** (real offsets) that overlays + wins; a rejected highlight writes a **suppression** the resolver subtracts; change-boundaries **materializes** that one occurrence — incremental, **no backfill**, DM-IH-1's rename-free/edit-robust properties preserved (*rejected:* (A) materialize-all = a migration + discards those properties; (C) alias-only = can't do change-boundaries or single-occurrence un-tag). **DM-S3c-2 = both attach-existing AND create-new-entity** (a new human-reached graph writer — INV-9 enumeration grows; needed to catch an entity extraction missed). **DM-S3c-3** occurrence-level (not-an-entity suppresses; not-this-entity suppresses + optional atomic re-tag); **DM-S3c-4** materialize-then-edit; **DM-S3c-5** tag/un-tag/boundary **ride the S3b `graph_edits` undo** (new op-kinds + inverters, contract-tested from writer output per the PR-#108 lesson); **DM-S3c-6** add `source`+`mention_id` to `ReaderHighlight`; **DM-S3c-7 = ADOPT TIPTAP NOW — owner override** of my native-selection lean (pay the editor setup so V2 §4 editing inherits a robust selection/decoration engine; Tiptap = a new fe dep → `/add-dependency` at the fe build; the `<mark>` renderer becomes Tiptap read-only + ProseMirror decorations); **DM-S3c-8** split be/fe; **DM-S3c-9 = no §3.5 *capability* amendment** (the S3a precedent — §3.5 already specifies manual tagging + the three corrections), storage model + INV-9 reword land in **ADR 0008** at build, with a small **§6.4 data-model note** (human-authored mentions carry real offsets) via stop-and-amend if the migration needs it. **Checks:** docs/vault only — no code, no deps.
- **2026-06-22 — Session 43 (M4.S3b-fe built + merged, PR #107; backend merge-undo bug fixed, PR #108) — M4.S3b COMPLETE.** The frontend for graph mutations, plus a bug its smoke surfaced. **(1) Undo affordance lives in the reader *header*, not the entity panel (owner call).** Undo is *story*-scoped (`POST …/graph-edits/undo` reverses the last edit *anywhere* in the story), so a per-entity placement would be semantically wrong. **(2) Property-conflict resolution is computed *client-side* from both entities' `properties`, not from the merge 400.** The merge route's 409/400 conflict body is a plain `{detail: string}` naming only the conflicting *keys* — no values — so a by-hand "pick which value to keep" resolver can't be driven from it; `mergeConflicts.buildConflictRows` mirrors the backend's pure `detect_property_conflicts` over both entities' fetched properties, and the 400 stays a safety net. *Considered & rejected:* round-trip the 400 then fetch values anyway (a wasted round-trip + a fragile string-parse). **(3) `useUndo` invalidates caches only on a *real* apply, never on a preview** (a preview touches nothing). **(4) The merge-undo 500 was op-name drift, fixed in PR #108 (split out, not scope-crept into the FE PR):** the merge writer records `op="discard_self_loop_relation"` (`_merge_rows`, `f"{kind}_relation"`) but `graph_undo.invert_operation` matched the bare `"discard_self_loop"`, so a self-loop-dropping merge's undo raised `UndoNotInvertible` → unhandled → 500 (delete-undo and self-loop-free merges were fine). CI stayed green because the inverter's unit test *hand-built* a fixture with the op name the writer never emits. **Fix:** match the real op + a **writer↔inverter contract test driven from real `_merge_rows` output** (closes the gap); the misleading fixture corrected to the real name (now a true regression). **No spec amendment** (ADR 0007 already covers the contract). **(5) Review-queue cross-cutting nits NOT discharged** — the S42 handoff optimistically said S3b-fe would discharge the "review-UX folds" note, but the reader-editing slices (S3a/S3b-fe) never touched the extraction/relation *review queues*, so the `CandidateView` merge-target-name / per-screen error-mapper / shared-`useReviewQueue` nits remain open (they fire only when a *review queue* next changes). **Retro:** two rules added — (a) `backend/src/story_forge/AGENTS.md`: test a string-coupled producer↔consumer contract from the producer's *real* output, not a hand-built fixture (the general form of the §2 fabricated-fixture lesson); (b) `frontend/AGENTS.md`: during a live smoke, use a `git worktree` for a parallel hotfix rather than `git checkout`-ing the working tree off the branch under test. **Checks:** 460 backend pass + ruff/`mypy --strict` clean; frontend build/lint/test green (247); CI green on both PRs; both review gates ran on #107; owner gave the per-merge OK on #108 and #107; merge/delete/undo verified live in the browser.
- **2026-06-20 — Session 42 (M4.S3b-be2 built + merged, PR #105): whole-entity delete + the general undo executor — INV-3 *executed*.** The first slice that *reverses* recorded graph operations. **(1) DM-S3b-5 survivor-delete confirmed (owner): allow + drift-refuse.** Deleting an entity that is an earlier merge's survivor is allowed unconditionally; if that merge's undo is later attempted, its drift-check refuses (409). No "is this a survivor?" guard on delete — the consistency check is pushed to undo, which already has a drift mechanism. *Considered & rejected:* block-the-delete (adds a survivor-lookup to every delete + a new failure mode for a window drift-refuse already covers). **(2) Re-do-after-undo id collision resolved = a generation discriminator** (the ADR 0007 design point). The deterministic `uuid5` operation id (keyed on the operation's targets, for crash-retry idempotency) collides if the *same* targets are re-operated after an undo recreates them. The build **kept the `undone_at` stamp model** and suffixes the seed with a generation = count of *undone* ops for those targets (`_op_seed`/`_next_generation`); a *live* op probes False so a retry re-derives the same id (idempotent), only an undone prior op bumps it. Applies to re-merge **and** re-delete. *Considered & rejected:* the ADR's delete-the-undone-rows alternative (discards the audit trail, contradicts the stamp model the be1 schema was built for). **(3) Layering:** pure `domain/graph_undo.invert_operation` (rows → ordered inverse plan + declarative drift check, reverse-`seq`) ; I/O in `EntityEditService.delete_entity`/`undo_last`; read path `PostgresEditStore.latest_live_operation` (COALESCE `operation_id`→`id` so S3a singletons are undoable — they now also carry `project_id`) / `mark_operation_undone`. INV-3 *executed* in `invariants.md`; INV-9 fifth witnessed instance (the undo executor *reverses* via the same human-reached writers — adds no new writer); `state-machines/graph-operation.md` (`applied → undone`) drawn. **(4) `/code-review` (multi-agent) caught a real data-loss bug `/review-pr` missed** — `fold_relation` undo issued `RemoveRelation(new_edge.id)` where the folded id is A's *pre-existing* edge, so undoing a merge that folded an edge deleted A's own edge (reachable when two merged entities share a relation to a common neighbour). **Folded** + two sibling undo-correctness fixes surfaced the same pass: a folded `add_relation` undo no longer deletes the pre-existing edge (the add now records `merged_into_existing`), and `remove_relation` undo restores the *full* edge (its before-image is now a full `model_dump`, not subject/predicate/object only — exact confidence/properties; the inverter still tolerates legacy thin rows). **(5) Undo/delete V1 robustness deferred → `docs/BACKLOG.md`** (owner ask, "note what should be done to make it more robust"): undo depth cap; one `created_at` per operation (clock-independent stack head); undo should *report* what open-world churn left unrestored; harden the delete snapshot against a mid-delete crash; collapse `_merge_rows`/`_delete_rows`; O(1) generation lookup. **No spec amendment** — §3.4 (delete) + §10 q2 (undo) were amended in S39; ADR 0007 covers the contract (re-merge resolution recorded into its Consequences). **Checks:** 459 backend pass + ruff/`mypy --strict` clean; frontend build/lint/test green; CI green; both review gates ran; owner gave the per-merge OK.
- **2026-06-20 — Session 41 (governance only — PLAN_SHORT slimming; no feature code).** **(1) `PLAN_SHORT.md` policy tightened to *current-milestone-only*** (owner). The Session-39 rule kept "current + immediately-prior milestone's Done tail", but even one prior milestone left the file at ~365 KB — over the **256 KB single-read limit** (it could no longer be read in one pass). Owner directed: PLAN_SHORT carries the **current milestone only**; all older milestones live in `docs/PLAN_ARCHIVE.md`, archived-and-referenced, **as a standing milestone-roll ritual step** (not a one-off). *Considered & rejected:* keeping M3 as "prior context" (still over the limit); a harder mid-milestone prune of struck cross-cutting/Blocked items (error-prone — deferred to the roll's §3 re-curation, where the whole list is walked anyway). **(2) `docs/AGENTS.md` §7 amended** to match (current-only; archive convention = newest-batch-on-top, verbatim reverse-chron within a batch; what-never-moves clarified). **(3) Ritual wired** (owner, raised S39): `/wrap-session` **step 5c** does/offers the roll-time archive move; `/resume-session` **step 3d** flags bloat (>~200 KB) as a backstop. **(4) First archive batch executed:** M3 + M2 + M1/M0 task sections, Decided, and Done → `docs/PLAN_ARCHIVE.md` (move-not-delete, §4; verified byte-for-byte — dated-bullet count 116 = 18 kept + 98 archived, no duplicates). `PLAN_SHORT.md` **368 KB → ~134 KB**. **Checks:** docs/governance only — no code, no deps; code gates n/a.
- **2026-06-20 — Session 40 (M4.S3b-be1 built + merged, PR #102).** The first M4.S3b backend slice — entity↔entity **merge** — shipped. **(1) Scope: be1 (merge) only** (owner-chosen — took the pre-authorized be1/be2 cut up front; the by-hand property-conflict resolution DM-S3b-2 enlarged merge, and undo can't be tested until merge first writes grouped rows). Delete + the undo executor are **be2**. **(2) Two build-time refinements beyond the resolved register, recorded in ADR 0007:** (a) `graph_edits` gained a **`project_id` column** so the undo stack is project-scoped (the resolved register didn't name it); (b) `repoint_entity_mentions` **returns the moved mention ids** (`RETURNING id`) so the before-image re-points *exactly* those rows back on undo (INV-3 completeness). **(3) Write order refined at build (the `/code-review` fold): delete B *last*** — fold A + re-point edges → re-point mentions → delete B → evidence. The resolved DM-S3b-4 said "Neo4j-then-Postgres"; deleting B first opened a window where its mentions were orphaned and the retry hit `EntityNotFound` (unrecoverable), so the build keeps B alive until the final graph write (still serving DM-S3b-4's retryable-not-half-merge intent); evidence rows reordered to match so undo recreates B before re-pointing mentions. **(4) Known be2 design point (ADR 0007):** the deterministic `uuid5(merge:B:A)` operation id collides if the same pair is re-merged after a be2 undo recreates B — undo must delete an undone op's rows (or add a nonce). **(5) `/review-pr` folds:** dedupe incident edges (a self-loop is returned twice by the undirected neighbourhood query); restrict `resolved_properties` to detected conflict keys (no silent property injection). **ADR 0007** landed (owner-confirmed); INV-9 grep guard widened (+`delete_entity`); INV-3 grouped-log note; relation/candidate lifecycle notes extended. *Considered & not done:* generalizing `_merge_rows` for be2 (YAGNI until be2 lands), parallelizing the neighbourhood reads (PoC scale). **Checks:** 427 backend pass + ruff/mypy clean; frontend lint/build/test clean; CI green; both review gates ran.

- **2026-06-19 — Session 37 (M4.S3a-be built + merged, PR #96).** **(1) DM-S3a-3 resolved-at-build to a *direct* edge-writer (option b) — the one decision that changed from the register's recorded lean.** The register's first choice routed a manual relation-add through `RelationReviewService.decide` to keep it the sole edge-writer; at build the `verify-at-build` falsified that — `decide` resolves an edge's endpoints by **surface-name-within-a-paragraph** (`_resolve` keys on `(paragraph_id, normalized_name)`), which a hand-picked edge between two arbitrary accepted entities has neither of, so a synthetic `staged_relations` row would mean fabricating a paragraph + names that round-trip to the chosen ids. - **2026-06-18 — Session 33 (M3→M4 vault sync + M4.S1 frontend reader + live smoke test + a backlog-file process change).** **(1) Vault-first, then build (owner).** Cleared the carried open-block B before any code: a `meta-architect:*` vault pass (PR #85) drew `state-machines/relation-lifecycle.md` (closes OQ-20), flipped `proposals/m4-inline-highlights.md` → `accepted` + annotated the DM-IH register resolved-as-built (OQ-21), fixed the `glossary/model-tier-routing.md` "not yet built" drift; the honest subtlety recorded: `held`/`committable` are *derived views* of the persisted `staged` row, not enum values. **(2) DM-IH-5 = reader-local fixed palette + hash fallback + legend (owner).** The graph viewer keeps its own pure-hash colouring, so a long-tail type may colour differently across the two linked views — *considered & rejected:* a shared colour module (would re-colour the shipped graph; beyond the surgical reader slice). - **2026-06-18 — Session 32 (M4.S1 backend + python-multipart waiver drop): inline-highlights span resolution decided by verifying the data first; the read-only backend shipped; a soak-date-floor rule folded.** **(1) DM-IH-1 — span resolution = render-time string search over name + aliases (owner, after a verify-first detour).** The owner chose "decide after I verify" over committing to an option blind; the verification settled it: the accept path (`candidate_review.py`) writes the mention with **null** `span_start/end`, the staged candidate carries no offset, and the spaCy `CandidateSpan` lives on a separate unlinked path — so the proposal's option (b) "persist the span we already have" was **illusory** (there is no span at accept time). And aliases *accumulate* the prose's surface forms (every merge-accept calls `add_alias(target, candidate_name)`), so an inflected form that was itself extracted+merged becomes a searchable alias — render-time search over canonical + aliases is materially stronger than the decompose assumed. *Considered & rejected:* persist-spans-now (no span to persist; a backend+data change in the slice the owner picked *because* it was low-risk UI), and a verify-build-measure hybrid up front (the verify already answered it). **(2) DM-IH-3 = plain `<mark>` renderer** (owner) — Tiptap/ProseMirror arrives with the manual-annotation slice where editing begins; *rejected:* adopt Tiptap now (ceremony ahead of need for a read-only view). **(3) DM-IH-2/4/7/8 built as proposed** — story-scoped `GET /stories/{id}/reader` doing the cross-store join + a tooltip catalog of only the entities that appeared; longest-match overlap; accepted-only (the read-side echo of INV-1, since mentions are written only by the accept path); tooltip = name+type+aliases. **DM-IH-5/6 (colour, perf)** deferred to the frontend slice (confirm-at-build). **No spec amendment** — §3.5 already specifies the reader; the slice is a read-only projection. **(4) `/code-review` caught a real crash `/review-pr` missed (5th consecutive substantive PR — #36/#60/#63/#78/#81):** the resolver matched against a *casefolded copy* of the paragraph, but casefold can change length on an expanding codepoint (ß→ss, İ→i̇), pushing an offset past the original text → `IndexError`/500 on the whole reader endpoint. Fixed by matching against the **original** text via `re.IGNORECASE` (+ `re.escape` so a name's regex metachars stay literal); regression-tested. **(5) python-multipart OSV waiver dropped (PR #82)** — the S31-deferred fix-first drop: 0.0.31 cleared its 14-day soak, bumped via `/add-dependency`, `GHSA-v9pg-7xvm-68hf` removed from `osv-scanner.toml` + `WAIVERS.md`; OSV scan clean, nothing unmasked. **(6) Retro (1 change, owner approved — soak-date floor):** a dated "drop when (soaks)" must be a **floor** = fixed-version publication date **+ (soak_days + 1)** (package + **15**, image + **8**), because the age gate (`check_dependency_age.py`: `NOW − 14d`) is **time-precise to the second** while a bare `+14` date is intra-day optimistic — this session a 0.0.31 published 06-04 08:27 UTC was still ~53 min too young at the recorded 06-18 drop date. Folded into `/triage-advisory` step 3 + the `infra/osv/WAIVERS.md` header. *Considered & rejected:* a "re-check on the drop day" note (weaker — still surprises); retro-editing the existing starlette dates (the drop-revisit re-runs the real age check anyway). The two other lessons **confirmed existing rules** (no change): `/code-review`-for-substantive-code worked (caught the crash), and verify-first (the deterministic-over-LLM instinct) paid off. **Reviews:** `/review-pr` (self) + `/code-review` (high, 7-angle); 347 backend tests green; both PRs CI 4/4 green, squash-merged.

The **owner browser smoke** walked every flow (tag existing/new, not-an-entity, not-this-entity + re-assign, change-boundaries with no ghost duplicate, undo) and confirmed all work; it surfaced that a manual tag's surface form shows in the panel's **Occurrences** timeline (not aliases) — working-as-designed — plus two post-PoC UX items now in `docs/BACKLOG.md` (type-field hints; surface manual forms as aliases/known-forms). **Next: M4 narrowed multi-story** — but first the §3.6/§9 stop-and-amend (world-graph OUT, multi-story narrowed) + a decompose of the slice. **Checks:** frontend 285 pass + lint/format/build clean; no deps changed; CI green on all four jobs; browser smoke passed; owner gave the per-merge OK. `/retro` skipped (owner).
- **2026-06-22 — Session 47: M4.S3c-fe1 shipped — reader migrated to a read-only Tiptap editor + ProseMirror decorations (PR #115, merged).** The first half of the reader's manual-correction frontend, split (owner's call) into a render-engine swap (this) and the correction UI (fe2). The reader's per-paragraph `<mark>` renderer is replaced by a single **read-only Tiptap editor** that draws accepted-entity highlights as ProseMirror **decorations** — a render-time overlay, so the prose is never rewritten — at **behavioural parity** (colour-by-type, hover tooltip, click + keyboard Enter/Space to open the side panel, occurrence-drill flash); **no write paths**. Why adopt a full editor for a read-only view (DM-S3c-7, owner override): the V2 editing modes inherit the engine, and fe2 can map a text selection back to (paragraph, offset) through the document model rather than the fragile rendered DOM. Built test-first where it counts: pure modules `readerDoc` (paragraphs → a Tiptap doc, one paragraph node per paragraph carrying its id) and `decorations` (the **verify-at-build** — converting the backend's Python *codepoint* offsets to ProseMirror's *UTF-16* positions against the original text, with an explicit emoji test — plus the decoration attributes); `ReaderEditor` is the isolated ProseMirror mount (no unit test, mocked in the container test, verified by the browser smoke — the same boundary as the graph's cytoscape canvases). Removed `ParagraphText` + `segments`. The browser parity smoke earned its keep: it caught a real bug unit tests structurally couldn't — Enter/Space did nothing because ProseMirror's `handleKeyDown` is an *edit* handler it skips on a read-only view; the fix moves key activation to a React handler. **Both review gates ran:** `/review-pr` flagged the keyboard parity + a defensive empty-document guard; the heavier `/code-review` confirmed **zero correctness bugs** in the offset math/reactive sync and surfaced a tooltip-fallback parity nit + a duplicate type + thinner test coverage — all folded. New dependency `@tiptap/*==3.26.0` (newest 3.x clearing the §6.7 14-day soak, OSV-clean, prod-audit clean). **Next: M4.S3c-fe2** — selection→offset, the right-click correction menu, the tag picker + new-entity form, and the three mutation hooks, on top of this editor. **Checks:** frontend 246 pass + lint/format/build clean; dep-age green; CI green on all four jobs; browser parity smoke passed; owner gave the per-merge OK. `/retro` skipped (owner).
- **2026-06-22 — Session 46: spec §6.4 reconciled — `entity_mentions.embedding vector(768)` added to the sketch (PR #113, merged; docs-only).** A short dedicated session (owner sequenced it before M4.S3c-fe) closing the S45-surfaced follow-up: the §6.4 Postgres data-model sketch had never gained the per-mention `embedding` column that M3 migration `cf0a36d67a73` added back in M3.S2. Before editing, **verified the column is genuinely used** (owner's challenge — "are we using them, or just here to be here?"): it's written on every accept and read back to feed the §3.3 **Stage-2** matcher (max-cosine of a candidate's context vector against an entity's stored mention vectors), in both the initial dedupe cascade and the on-accept re-match. So **per-mention embeddings are an in-PoC, load-bearing capability**, not an unused feature — the only problem was the sketch lagging the live schema. Fix was spec-only (the sketch line + a short "Per-mention context vector" note on purpose/provenance/nullability); a documentation-accuracy reconcile, not a capability change. No code, deps, or migration touched. `/retro` skipped (owner's call — the reflective pass found the verify-before-document instinct already covered by existing discipline). **Next: M4.S3c-fe** — the Tiptap read-only reader + selection + right-click correction menu + tag picker (DM-S3c-7). **Checks:** docs only — backend/frontend gates n/a; CI green on all four jobs for PR #113; owner gave the per-merge OK.
- **2026-06-22 — Session 45: M4.S3c-be shipped — manual tag / un-tag / change-boundaries backend (PR #111, merged).** The backend for "manual correction in the reader" (spec §3.5) — the last of the three write-risk-sliced families (S3a edit · S3b merge/delete/undo · **S3c**). The dominating problem the M4.S1 design left: a rendered highlight is a *live search hit with no saved identity*, so a hand-tagged span (an inflected form, a pronoun, a brand-new entity) can't be re-found by search and "this highlight is wrong" has no row to delete. The resolved model — **"save only what you touch"** — keeps the live search for auto highlights and adds, incrementally, only what the author actually touches: a manual tag persists a **stored span** (real char offsets, marked `source='manual'`) that overlays and wins over search; a rejected highlight writes a **suppression** record the resolver subtracts; changing a boundary on a search hit *materializes* just that occurrence. No data migration, and the M4.S1 "rename re-highlights for free" behaviour is preserved. Built test-first: a **pure reconciling resolver** (`reconcile_highlights` = search ∪ manual − suppressions, manual-wins-then-longest-match — the first failing test); a **§6.4 schema amendment** (a `source` column + a `mention_suppressions` table, taken through the stop-and-amend flow first); five write operations on the existing edit service (**tag an existing entity, tag a brand-new entity, "not an entity", "not this entity", change boundaries**); and full **undo** integration — every correction is reversible through the existing story-scoped Undo, with the inverters **tested against the writer's real recorded output** (not a hand-built fixture) so a producer/consumer drift can't hide. Tagging can **create a new accepted entity** directly (a new human-reached graph writer — INV-9's enumeration grows, its sixth witnessed instance). `ADR 0008` records the storage model + the reconciliation contract; INV-9 reconciled across the vault. **Both review gates ran:** the self-review found nothing blocking; the heavier multi-agent `/code-review` found **zero correctness bugs** and surfaced one cleanup (a deterministic-id formula repeated four times — folded into a shared helper so undo-by-id can't drift). One build-time refinement, recorded in the ADR: rejection is handled **uniformly as a suppression** (even over a manual tag) rather than deleting rows — one mechanism, one inverse. **Surfaced a follow-up** (owner ask): the §6.4 schema sketch omits the `entity_mentions.embedding` column M3 already added — to be reconciled, and its PoC scope decided, in its own near-term session (Blocked/questions). **Next: M4.S3c-fe** — the Tiptap read-only reader + selection + right-click menu + tag picker (DM-S3c-7), the slice that makes all of this usable in the browser. **Checks:** backend 523 pass + ruff/`mypy --strict` clean; frontend 247 pass + lint/format/build clean; CI green on all four jobs; owner gave the per-merge OK.
- **2026-06-22 — Session 44: M4.S3c scoped + decomposed + register RESOLVED; M4 multi-story scope re-cut (design/planning only — no production code).** The next slice's full design pass, plus owner scope decisions that reshaped the rest of M4. **(1) M4.S3c — manual tag / un-tag / change-boundaries decomposed** (`meta-architect:decompose-requirement` step-0 → `architecture/proposals/m4-s3c-manual-tagging.md`, `accepted`, register **DM-S3c-1..9 / OQ-26 RESOLVED**). It's the final "manual correction in the reader" slice (after S3a edit + S3b merge/delete/undo). The dominating finding: a rendered highlight today is a render-time **search hit with no saved identity** (the M4.S1 design left `entity_mentions` offsets NULL and searches the prose live), so a manually-tagged span (an inflected form, a pronoun, a brand-new entity) can't be re-found by search, and "this highlight is wrong" has no stored row to delete. **Owner resolved the storage model = "save only what you touch"** (keep the live search for auto highlights; persist real offsets only for spots tagged/corrected by hand; record a small suppression note for a rejected highlight — incremental, no data migration, the M4.S1 "rename re-highlights for free" behaviour preserved), plus: tagging can **create new entities** (not just attach to existing), corrections are **undoable** via the existing story-scoped Undo, and — overriding the architect's lean — **adopt the Tiptap editor now** so the V2 text-editing features inherit a robust selection engine. New glossary term `materialization`; the storage model + the INV-9 enumeration growth land in **ADR 0008** at build (no §3.5 capability amendment — §3.5 already specifies manual tagging; a small §6.4 data-model note if the migration needs it). **(2) M4 multi-story re-scoped (owner):** the **world-graph** layer (cross-story world merge, §3.6) is **dropped from the PoC** → `docs/BACKLOG.md` (reversing the prior "basic world-graph is in-PoC" note); what stays is the narrower **"add a new story that reuses the existing project graph + per-story entity membership"** (which entity appears in which story — drives the §3.4 "this story / whole world" toggle *and* lets known entities seed extraction in a new story). The spec §3.6/§9 still describe the world graph — a **stop-and-amend is flagged** before that slice is built. **(3) New backlog item: code-documentation generation** (first stone toward living, source-derived project docs). **(4) Retro → one rule added (owner-approved):** root `AGENTS.md` "How to communicate" — when surfacing a decision-register entry for the owner to resolve, translate it to plain language, never lift the register's architect-shorthand into the question (earned this session: the first attempt at the storage-model question was jargon-packed and unparseable; re-asked plainly, it was immediately clear). **Gap-check (owner-requested):** ran the `/review-pr` §2 reconciliation sweep over the docs/vault diff — caught + fixed a stale `PLAN_SHORT` Decided entry still calling the S3c register "OPEN" (the authoritative home of the resolutions) and two stale forward-references to the now-dropped world graph. **Checks:** docs/vault only — no code, no deps; backend/frontend gates are no-ops. **Next: build M4.S3c-be test-first** — first failing test = the pure reconciling-resolver (search hits ∪ saved manual spans − suppressions → final highlight ranges); then the tag/un-tag/boundary mutators + endpoints + the new undo op-kinds; then M4.S3c-fe brings in Tiptap (via `/add-dependency`). - **2026-06-22 — Session 43: M4.S3b-fe shipped — merge/delete/undo reader UI (PR #107, merged) — and a backend merge-undo bug it surfaced, fixed (PR #108, merged). M4.S3b is COMPLETE end-to-end.** The frontend for the graph-mutation routes, test-first in the S3a-fe rhythm (pure mapper → hook → component): `mergeConflicts.ts` (by-hand property-conflict resolver computed *client-side* from both entities' properties, because the merge 400 carries only conflicting key names, not values — mirrors the backend's `detect_property_conflicts`); `useMergeEntities`/`useDeleteEntity`/`useUndo` (undo invalidates the reader/graph/detail caches only on a *real* apply, never on a preview); `MergeControls` (reuse `EntityPicker` → conflict resolver → confirm → `MergeSummaryResponse` counts; self-merge blocked client-side); delete-with-confirm in `ReaderEntityPanel` (closes the panel on success); `UndoButton` in the reader *header* (undo is **story-scoped** — owner call) with preview→confirm→apply and 404 (nothing to undo) / 409 (drift) handling. CI had stayed green because the inverter's unit test hand-built a fixture with the op name the writer never emits. Fixed in PR #108 (split out as its own backend PR, not scope-crept into the FE PR): match the real op + a **writer↔inverter contract test driven from real `_merge_rows` output**, and the misleading fixture corrected to the real name (now a true regression). Verified live after the fix: merge→undo (magistrate restored), re-merge, and delete→undo all work. **Retro → two rules added (owner-approved):** (a) `backend/src/story_forge/AGENTS.md` — test a string-coupled producer↔consumer contract from the producer's *real* output, not a hand-built fixture of the string (the producer/consumer generalisation of the `/review-pr` §2 fabricated-fixture lesson, which had only covered HTTP-status/LLM-schema fixtures); (b) `frontend/AGENTS.md` — during a live smoke, use a `git worktree` for a parallel hotfix rather than `git checkout`-ing the working tree off the branch under test (mid-smoke the checkout flipped the reader to `main` and the buttons vanished). **Note:** the S42 handoff's claim that S3b-fe would discharge the "review-UX folds" cross-cutting nits was optimistic — the reader-editing slices never touched the extraction/relation *review queues*, so those nits stay open. **Checks:** 460 backend pass + ruff/`mypy --strict` clean; frontend 247 pass + build/lint/format clean; CI green on both PRs; owner gave the per-merge OK on each.
- **2026-06-20 — Session 42: M4.S3b-be2 shipped — whole-entity delete + the general undo executor (PR #105, merged). INV-3 moves from *recorded* to *executed*.** be1 wrote the grouped, append-only `graph_edits` log; be2 consumes it. **Delete:** `EntityEditService.delete_entity` removes an accepted entity, its relations, and its text occurrences (real `DETACH DELETE` + a full before-image snapshot — node + incident edges + mentions), recorded as one grouped reversible operation; `DELETE /stories/{id}/entities/{eid}` (204/404/503). **Undo:** `undo_last` → `POST …/graph-edits/undo` (undo-last) reverses the newest live operation — reads it, inverts it in reverse `seq` via the pure `domain/graph_undo.invert_operation`, runs a drift check (refuse → 409 if the target was edited/re-created since), applies each inverse through the same human-reached writers, then stamps it `undone`; `?preview=true` reports *what would be reversed* without acting (DM-S3b-1 see-what-I-undo). Read path: `PostgresEditStore.latest_live_operation` (project-scoped; `COALESCE(operation_id, id)` so S3a singleton edits are undoable too) + `mark_operation_undone`. **Two design points from ADR 0007 settled:** DM-S3b-5 survivor-delete = allow + drift-refuse (owner-confirmed); the re-do-after-undo `uuid5` id collision = a generation discriminator that keeps the `undone_at` stamp model (recorded back into ADR 0007's Consequences). **Architecture:** INV-3 *executed* + INV-9 fifth witnessed instance in `invariants.md`; new `state-machines/graph-operation.md` (`applied → undone`); INDEX updated. **Reviews — the two-gate rule paid off again (6th+ substantive PR):** `/review-pr` (self) flagged the doc reconciliation + crash-window notes; **`/code-review` (multi-agent, high) caught a real data-loss bug** — `fold_relation` undo deleted the survivor's pre-existing edge — plus two sibling undo-fidelity issues, all folded with regression tests (incl. a fold-undo integration test). Undo/delete V1 robustness items (depth cap, clock-independent stack head, unrestored-churn signal, mid-delete-crash hardening, row-factory dedup) recorded in `docs/BACKLOG.md` at the owner's request. **Checks:** 459 backend pass + ruff/`mypy --strict` clean; frontend build/lint/test green; CI green. **Lesson:** the documented "run `/code-review` in addition to `/review-pr` on substantive destructive write-paths because a missed bug is costly and the Codex net is thin" rule earned its keep yet again — the fold data-loss bug was exactly the cross-file/edge-case class a single self-review structurally can't catch. **Next: M4.S3b-fe** (merge flow UI + delete-with-confirm + an undo affordance that previews what it reverses). **Retro → one ritual tightening (owner-approved): neutral waiver-soak framing in the handoff.** The resume brief misread the starlette waivers as "soaked / actionable" when their drop-floor dates were days in the *future* — caused by the prior handoff's pre-judged "DUE THIS WEEK / should have soaked by now" wording (the soak-equivalent of a false infra anchor — it goes stale, and acting on it bumps a dep still inside its 14-day soak, a §6.7 misstep). Fixed both halves: **`/wrap-session` step 7** now requires waiver lines to state a *neutral floor date to compute against* ("droppable on YYYY-MM-DD"), never a verdict; **`/resume-session` step 3b** now says compute drop-readiness from the floor date vs today, don't inherit the handoff's framing. *Considered & rejected:* a rule for the pre-commit `ruff-format`-aborts-a-commit micro-friction (self-correcting — the hook is its own safety net). The two-gate review catching the fold data-loss bug *confirmed* the existing rule (no change).

The archive move is queued (cross-cutting) for a future wrap. **Checks:** docs/vault/spec only — no backend/frontend code, no deps; code gates n/a. **Lessons:** (a) running the architecture re-sync *before* the decompose (so the architect reads current state) is the right order at a slice boundary — the resume handoff called it and it paid off; (b) when a decompose names a spec section for an amendment, verify the section's *current content* fits before asserting it — the "delete → §3.5" inheritance was wrong (§3.5 is mention-level) and was caught at spec-sign-off, not before; (c) when the owner flags a *recurring* hygiene problem ("better than accumulation"), encode a durable rule, not just a one-off task. **Retro → one skill tightening (owner-approved):** lesson (b) was encoded into **`meta-architect:decompose-requirement`** — a register entry naming a *spec section* as a decision's home/amendment target is a hypothesis until that section is read (the spec analogue of the existing `verify-at-build` rule for un-inspected external-tool behaviour); the §3.5→§3.4 delete miss is the worked example.
- **2026-06-20 — Session 38: M4.S3a-fe shipped — the editable entity side panel (PR #98, merged); M4.S3a is complete.** The reader's entity side panel, read-only since M4.S2b, now **edits** committed graph state — the first reader→graph mutation UI. **What landed (test-first, mirroring S2a/S2b pure-mapper → hook → component):** three mutation hooks (`useEntityEdit` PATCH, `useAddRelation` POST, `useRemoveRelation` DELETE) + `patchJsonBody`/204-safe `del` client helpers, each invalidating the reader + graph + entity-detail queries on success (DM-S3a-4 — a corrected name re-highlights / a new type recolours for free via render-time search); a pure `propertiesEditor.ts` (typed string/number/bool rows, nested/array/null preserved as read-only JSON — DM-S3a-5, free keys INV-4); and `ReaderEntityPanel` gaining an Edit mode (name/type/aliases/typed properties) + a relations add (reusing the M3.S4d `EntityPicker`, DM-S3a-8)/remove section that surfaces the `merged_into_existing` collision flag as a warning. - **2026-06-18 — Session 32: M4.S1 inline-highlights **backend** shipped (PR #81) + the python-multipart OSV waiver dropped (PR #82).** The first M4 ("V1 polish") feature code, the read-only side of inline highlights (spec §3.5). **(1) Resolved the DM-IH register with the owner by verifying the data first.** The owner chose "decide after I verify" on the gating call (DM-IH-1 span resolution); the verification found the accept path writes the mention with **null** char offsets and the spaCy span is gone by accept time — so the decompose's "persist the existing span" option was *illusory* — while aliases accumulate the prose's actual surface forms (each merge-accept adds one), making **render-time string search over canonical_name + aliases** both the only zero-data-change option *and* stronger on inflection than assumed. Folded into `/triage-advisory` step 3 + `infra/osv/WAIVERS.md`. **Checks:** 347 backend tests green; ruff/format/mypy/frontend-lint/tsc clean; both PRs CI 4/4 green, squash-merged (#81 `01b2173`, #82 `3f16d5e`). **Not done (carried to next session):** acting on the 2026-06-17 architecture report + OQ-20 (the relation-lifecycle state-machine drawing) + the `glossary/model-tier-routing.md` "not yet built" drift — a `meta-architect:*` vault pass. **Lessons:** (a) *verify before you commit to a design option* — the owner's "decide after I verify" turned a plausible-but-wrong choice (persist spans) into the right one (search) by reading the actual write path; the deterministic-over-LLM instinct, applied to a design decision; (b) `/code-review` caught a self-review miss for the **fifth** consecutive substantive PR — the casefold-length assumption was load-bearing and invisible to a happy-path read; the multi-agent finder's edge-case angle is the safety net the single self-review structurally lacks; (c) a recorded soak *date* is a floor, not the gate — the gate is time-precise, so date arithmetic that ignores the publication time-of-day surprises you by hours on the drop day.

- [x] ~~**DM-Rel-5: re-point a *written* relation edge on an accepted-entity↔entity merge (M4).**~~ ✅ **Resolved — shipped in M4.S3b-be1 (PR #102, Session 40); confirmed by a code re-verify + struck at the 2026-06-25 (Session 55) roll.** `domain/entity_merge.py` `plan_merge` re-points every edge incident to the absorbed entity B onto survivor A; because `relation_edge_id = uuid5(subject, predicate, object)` is content-addressed, a re-point is delete-old + create-new, a colliding id **folds** (MERGE-collapse, multiplicity reported), and a post-swap self-loop is discarded — wired through `EntityEditService.merge_entities`. _Original framing (kept as history):_ **DM-Rel-5: re-point a *written* relation edge on an accepted-entity↔entity merge (M4).** S4e writes edges *lazily* (resolve each endpoint to its candidate's committed id), so re-point "mostly dissolved" — *except* merging two **already-accepted** entities (which doesn't exist in M3) re-points the edges already written to the absorbed entity. M4's **properties/relations edit** + multi-story is where that merge first arrives, so this deferred case becomes live work then: on an entity↔entity merge, re-point (or `MERGE`-collapse, given the deterministic `uuid5(subject,predicate,object)` edge id) every edge touching the absorbed id onto the survivor. - ~~**LLM router doesn't record/fail-over on a malformed-but-`200` provider envelope.**~~ ✅ **Resolved 2026-06-08 (M2.S3, PR #42):** typed `ProviderResponseError` added in `adapters/llm/base.py`, raised by the Ollama + OpenRouter adapters on a malformed-`200` envelope (missing fields, unparseable body, **and null `content`** — the null case caught by `/code-review`), and `router.py` records a failure row + fails over like a 5xx; the "envelope-malformed vs schema-invalid" split is proven by router tests. Closes the §6.6 "one row per call" gap (INV-5). (M2.S2 own-review should-fix → built M2.S3.)
- ~~**ChunkingAgent doesn't map `ProviderResponseError` (malformed-`200`) to its route's 502.**~~ ✅ **Resolved 2026-06-10 (M2.S4, PR #48):** `ChunkingAgent` now catches `ProviderResponseError` around the provider call → `ChunkingError` (the structure route already maps that to 502), so a malformed-200 during chunking is a 502, not an unhandled 500. + test. Original below. M2.S3 added a typed `ProviderResponseError` (adapters raise it on a malformed-`200` envelope). `ExtractionAgent` is behind the router, which records + fails over; but `ChunkingAgent` holds a *raw* `OllamaProvider` and its retry loop catches only `ValidationError`, so a malformed-`200` during chunking propagates as `ProviderResponseError` past the route's `except ChunkingError` → an unhandled **500**, though `POST /stories/{id}/structure` advertises **502** for LLM failure. **Not a regression** (pre-M2.S3 the same body raised a raw `KeyError` → also 500). Cheap fix: catch `ProviderResponseError` in `ChunkingAgent` → `ChunkingError` (the route already maps that to 502). The deeper fix is to move chunking behind the router like extraction (gets failover + the `llm_calls` row too) — lands naturally with **M2.S4**. (M2.S3 `/code-review` finding, deferred 2026-06-08.)
- ~~**`RelationCandidate` accepts blank `subject`/`predicate`/`object` as success.**~~ ✅ **Resolved 2026-06-10 (M2.S4, PR #48):** added the same non-empty `field_validator` (covering all three fields) used for `candidate_name`, so blank relation output is retried not accepted; + an agent-retry test and a direct-validation test. Original below. `agents/extraction_agent.py:92-94` types the three relation fields as plain `str` with **no non-empty validator** (only `candidate_name` has one). A model returning `{"subject":"","predicate":"","object":"",…}` validates as a successful `ExtractionProposal`, so the agent's retry loop **stops** and the future M2.S4 graph writer gets a relation with no usable endpoint or type. **Distinct from the intentionally-accepted dangling relation** — a dangling endpoint still needs a *non-empty* surface form or id; only its *resolution* (match/create) is deferred to M3. Fix: add the same non-empty `field_validator` used for `candidate_name` to `subject`/`predicate`/`object`, so blank output is retried not accepted; + a test. A real gap **both** M2.S3 review passes missed (tests cover blank `candidate_name` + empty-lists, never blank relation fields). Small — fold into **M2.S4** (where it bites) or a quick standalone PR. (External review remark on merged PR #42, 2026-06-08.)
